\subsubsection*{Physics-bridge verification for gravity}

\begin{theorem}[Gravitational MC element; \ClaimStatusProvedHere]
\label{thm:gravity-mc}
\index{universal MC element!3d!gravitational}
$SL(2,\R)$ Chern--Simons theory at level~$k$ on $\R_+ \times \C$
lies in the scope of Theorem~\ref{thm:physics-bridge}.  The resulting
logarithmic $\SCchtop$-algebra determines an MC element
$\alpha_{\mathrm{grav}} \in \mc(\gSC_T)$ whose faces are:
\begin{enumerate}[label=\textup{(\roman*)}]
\item closed face $= \mathrm{Vir}_c$,
\item open face $= $ abstract line-side package
  \textup{(Theorem~\ref{thm:lines_as_modules})},
\item spectral $R$-matrix $= $ abstract line-side braiding,
\item genus face $= \Theta_{\mathrm{Vir}_c}$,
\item PVA descent $= \{T_\lambda T\}$.
\end{enumerate}
Items \textup{(i)--(v)} are proved unconditionally at the abstract
level.  The concrete identification of the open face with
$\mathrm{Vir}_{26-c}$-modules and of the spectral $R$-matrix with
the Virasoro fusion kernel is conjectural
\textup{(Remark~\ref{rem:gravity-mc-scope})}.
\end{theorem}

\begin{proof}
The gauge-fixed BV-BRST complex of Chern--Simons theory is cubic in
$A$, so the one-loop finiteness input of Theorem~\ref{thm:physics-bridge}
holds by power counting.  Its propagator is
$K(t,z) = \Theta(t)/(2\pi z)$, which has the required meromorphic
holomorphic behavior and ordered topological dependence.  The
interaction vertices are polynomial, so the renormalized
configuration-space integrals are precisely of the type covered by the
bridge theorem.  Hence the theory defines a logarithmic
$\SCchtop$-algebra.  Each listed projection of
$\alpha_{\mathrm{grav}}$ was computed in Movements~I--IV\@.
The abstract line-side package exists by
Theorem~\ref{thm:lines_as_modules}; its braiding is the abstract
spectral $R$-matrix of the bar complex.
\end{proof}

\begin{remark}[Scope: abstract vs.\ concrete line-side identifications]
\label{rem:gravity-mc-scope}
The open face and spectral $R$-matrix in
Theorem~\ref{thm:gravity-mc} are proved at the \emph{abstract}
level: the line-side package exists as the open-colour $E_1$-module
category of the bar complex, and the braiding is its abstract
spectral $R$-matrix.  The \emph{concrete} identification of this
package with highest-weight $\mathrm{Vir}_{26-c}$-modules and of the
braiding with the Virasoro fusion kernel is conjectural; see
Remark~\ref{rem:gravity-line-virasoro-realization} and
Conjecture~\ref{conj:gravity-line-identification}.
\end{remark}

\subsubsection*{BTZ black holes as MC deformations}

\begin{definition}[BTZ deformation]
\label{def:btz-deformation}
\index{BTZ black hole!as MC deformation}
A BTZ black hole of mass~$M$ and angular momentum~$J$ is a MC
deformation $\delta\alpha \in \gSC_T$ of $\alpha_{\mathrm{grav}}$,
satisfying $D_{\alpha_{\mathrm{grav}}}(\delta\alpha) = 0$,
corresponding to the highest-weight state $|h, \bar h\rangle$ with
$h = (M\ell + J)/2$, $\bar h = (M\ell - J)/2$.
\end{definition}

\subsubsection*{The Cardy formula: partition function and modular $S$-transform}

The genus-$1$ MC element $\Theta^{(1)}$ produces the boundary
partition function.  Write $q = e^{2\pi i\tau}$ for the modular
parameter of the boundary torus.  The categorical trace gives
\begin{equation}\label{eq:gravity-Z1}
Z_1(\tau)
\;=\;
\Tr_{\mathrm{Vir}_c}\!\left(q^{L_0 - c/24}\right)
\;=\;
\frac{q^{-c/24}}{\prod_{n=2}^{\infty}(1-q^n)},
\end{equation}
the product starting at $n = 2$ because $\mathrm{Vir}_c$ has no
weight-$1$ states.  The full partition function counting all states
at inverse temperature $\beta = 2\pi\,\mathrm{Im}\,\tau$ is
\begin{equation}\label{eq:gravity-Z-full}
Z(\tau,\bar\tau)
\;=\;
\sum_{h,\bar h}
d(h,\bar h)\,q^{h - c/24}\,\bar q^{\bar h - c/24}.
\end{equation}
Modular invariance $Z(-1/\tau, -1/\bar\tau) = Z(\tau,\bar\tau)$
and vacuum dominance in the high-temperature limit give
\begin{equation}\label{eq:gravity-vacuum-dominance}
Z(\tau,\bar\tau)
\;\sim\;
\exp\!\left(
  \frac{\pi c}{12}\cdot\frac{1}{\mathrm{Im}(-1/\tau)}
\right)
\qquad (\mathrm{Im}\,\tau \to 0^+).
\end{equation}
In the bar-complex language, the $S$-transform acts on
$\Theta_{\mathrm{grav}}$ by exchanging the two boundary cycles of
the genus-$1$ bordered FM compactification; vacuum dominance is
the statement that the arity-$0$ component
$\Theta^{(1)}_{n=0} = \kappa\cdot\omega_1$ controls the
exponential growth of states.

\subsubsection*{Saddle-point extraction and the Cardy formula}

The degeneracy $d(h)$ at large $h$ is extracted by inverse Laplace
transform from~\eqref{eq:gravity-vacuum-dominance}.  The
saddle-point of $f(\tau) = \pi c/(12\tau) + 2\pi\tau(h - c/24)$
is at
\begin{equation}\label{eq:gravity-saddle}
\tau_*
\;=\;
i\sqrt{\frac{c}{24(h - c/24)}}
\;\approx\;
i\sqrt{\frac{c}{24h}}
\qquad (h \gg c),
\end{equation}
giving $f(\tau_*) \approx 2\pi\sqrt{ch/6}$.

\begin{conjecture}[Cardy formula from the bar complex;
\ClaimStatusConjectured]
\label{conj:gravity-cardy}
\label{conj:cardy-mc}
\index{Cardy formula!from bar complex|textbf}
\index{BTZ black hole!Cardy formula}
The asymptotic entropy of the Virasoro bar complex at large
conformal weight is
\begin{equation}\label{eq:gravity-cardy}
\boxed{
S_{\mathrm{Cardy}}
\;=\;
2\pi\sqrt{\frac{c\,h}{6}}
\;+\;
2\pi\sqrt{\frac{c\,\bar h}{6}}.
}
\end{equation}
This is the logarithmic growth rate of MC deformations
of $\alpha_{\mathrm{grav}}$ at highest weight $(h,\bar h)$.
\end{conjecture}

\begin{remark}[Conditional derivation of the Cardy formula]
\label{rem:cardy-derivation}
The derivation rests on three bar-complex inputs:
\begin{enumerate}[label=(\roman*)]
\item The curvature $\kappa(\mathrm{Vir}_c) = c/2$ from the
  genus-$1$ self-loop, which determines
  $\Theta^{(1)}_{n=0} = \kappa\cdot\omega_1$ and hence the
  vacuum energy $-c/24$.
\item The modular invariance of $Z(\tau,\bar\tau)$, which
  follows from the consistency of the genus-$1$ MC equation
  on the moduli stack $\cM_{1,1}$: the modular group acts as
  autoequivalences of the bordered FM compactification, and
  the MC element is invariant under this action.
\item The saddle-point at
  $\tau_* = i\sqrt{c/(24h)}$~\eqref{eq:gravity-saddle},
  which follows from the analytic structure of the
  $S$-channel expansion.
\end{enumerate}
All three inputs are determined by the single datum
$\kappa = c/2$, itself determined by the quartic OPE pole in
$\{T_\lambda T\}$.  The Cardy formula is thus a consequence of
the curvature of the Virasoro bar complex.  The conjectural
step is the passage from algebraic modular invariance of the
MC element to the analytic modular invariance of the
partition function needed for the saddle-point extraction.
\end{remark}

\begin{remark}[Cardy growth rate in $\kappa$-variables]
\label{rem:cardy-thesis}
\index{Cardy formula!kappa variables}
The Cardy growth rate can be rewritten using
$\kappa(\mathrm{Vir}_c) = c/2$: the saddle weight
$2\pi\sqrt{ch/6}$ is $2\pi\sqrt{4\kappa h/6}
= 2\pi\sqrt{2\kappa h/3}$.  This rewriting is a notational
move, not a derivation: the Cardy formula itself is
Conjecture~\ref{conj:gravity-cardy} at the bar-complex level
(the conditional derivation is recorded in
Remark~\ref{rem:cardy-derivation}, whose analytic step
remains conjectural), and the thesis supplies no independent
input beyond the $\kappa$-identification.  What the
$\kappa$-form does record is that any class-$\mathbf{M}$ VOA
admitting a Cardy-type asymptotic under the same conjectural
analytic inputs would produce the analogous growth rate
governed by its own curvature; the specific Virasoro
constants are fixed by Brown--Henneaux
(Theorem~\ref{thm:brown-henneaux}), not by the thesis.
\end{remark}

\subsubsection*{BTZ entropy from the bar complex}

\begin{conjecture}[BTZ entropy; \ClaimStatusConjectured]
\label{conj:gravity-btz-entropy}
\index{BTZ black hole!entropy|textbf}
\index{Bekenstein--Hawking entropy!from bar complex}
The Bekenstein--Hawking entropy of the BTZ black hole is
\begin{equation}\label{eq:gravity-btz-entropy}
\boxed{
S_{\mathrm{BTZ}}
\;=\;
\frac{2\pi r_+}{4G}
\;=\;
2\pi\sqrt{\frac{c\,h}{6}}
\;+\;
2\pi\sqrt{\frac{c\,\bar h}{6}},
}
\end{equation}
where $c = 3\ell/(2G)$ is the Brown--Henneaux central charge
\textup{(}Theorem~\textup{\ref{thm:brown-henneaux})},
$h,\bar h$ are the left and right conformal weights,
and $r_+$ is the outer horizon radius.
Equivalently, $S_{\mathrm{BTZ}} = 2\pi\sqrt{\kappa h/3}
+ 2\pi\sqrt{\kappa\bar h/3}$ with $\kappa = c/2$.
\end{conjecture}

\begin{remark}[Conditional derivation of the BTZ entropy]
\label{rem:btz-derivation}
Assuming Conjecture~\ref{conj:gravity-cardy}, substitute
$c = 3\ell/(2G)$, $h = (M\ell+J)/2$,
$\bar h = (M\ell-J)/2$ into the Cardy
formula~\eqref{eq:gravity-cardy}:
\begin{align*}
S_{\mathrm{BTZ}}
&\;=\;
2\pi\sqrt{\frac{3\ell}{2G}\cdot\frac{M\ell+J}{12}}
\;+\;
2\pi\sqrt{\frac{3\ell}{2G}\cdot\frac{M\ell-J}{12}}
\\[4pt]
&\;=\;
\frac{2\pi\ell}{4G}\!\left(
  \sqrt{\frac{M\ell+J}{2}}
  +\sqrt{\frac{M\ell-J}{2}}
\right).
\end{align*}
In terms of the horizon radii
$r_\pm^2 = \ell^2(M\ell \pm J)/2$:
$S_{\mathrm{BTZ}} = 2\pi(r_+ + r_-)/(4G)$.
For $J=0$ (non-rotating BTZ), $r_+ = r_-$ and this reduces to
the standard Bekenstein--Hawking formula
$S = 2\pi r_+/(4G) = \mathrm{Area}/(4G)$ for the
one-dimensional horizon.
\end{remark}

\begin{remark}[BTZ entropy in $\kappa$-variables]
\label{rem:btz-thesis}
\index{BTZ black hole!kappa variables}
Conditional on Conjecture~\ref{conj:gravity-cardy} and on
Brown--Henneaux (Theorem~\ref{thm:brown-henneaux}), the BTZ
entropy can be reassembled in $\kappa$-variables.  A BTZ
black hole is declared to be an MC deformation
$\delta\alpha \in \gSC_T$ of $\alpha_{\mathrm{grav}}$
(Definition~\ref{def:btz-deformation}).  Substituting
$c = 2\kappa(\mathrm{Vir}_c)$ and the Brown--Henneaux value
$c = 3\ell/(2G_N)$ into the Cardy weight reproduces the area
law, as worked out in Remark~\ref{rem:btz-derivation}.  The
area-law coefficient $1/(4G_N)$ is \emph{not} fixed by the
chiral curvature: it is the Bekenstein--Hawking coefficient,
external to the bar complex, and appears here only because
it was already present in the Brown--Henneaux input.  What
the $\kappa$-reformulation does deliver is a notational
alignment between the boundary curvature and the bulk area
law, under the assumption that the Cardy conjecture and
Brown--Henneaux both hold in their usual forms.
\end{remark}

\subsubsection*{Verdier duality and the modular $S$-transform}

The Koszul involution $c \mapsto 26-c$ (Verdier duality
$\mathbb{D}$, Theorem~\ref{thm:gravity-verdier-intertwining})
and the modular $S$-transform $\tau \mapsto -1/\tau$ are
independent operations acting on different aspects of the MC
element.

\begin{proposition}[Commutativity of $\mathbb{D}$ and $S$;
\ClaimStatusProvedHere]
\label{prop:gravity-D-S-commute}
\index{Verdier duality!modular $S$-transform commutativity}
\index{modular $S$-transform!Verdier commutativity}
The Verdier involution $\mathbb{D}$ and the modular
$S$-transform commute on genus-$1$ MC elements:
\[
S \circ \mathbb{D}(\Theta_{\mathrm{Vir}_c}^{(1)}(\tau))
\;=\;
\mathbb{D} \circ S(\Theta_{\mathrm{Vir}_c}^{(1)}(\tau))
\;=\;
\Theta_{\mathrm{Vir}_{26-c}}^{(1)}(-1/\tau).
\]
\end{proposition}

\begin{proof}
$\mathbb{D}$ acts on algebraic data
($c \mapsto 26-c$, $\kappa \mapsto (26-c)/2$); $S$ acts on the
modular parameter ($\tau \mapsto -1/\tau$).  They act on different
variables and hence commute.
$\mathbb{D}(\Theta_{\mathrm{Vir}_c}^{(1)}(\tau))
= \Theta_{\mathrm{Vir}_{26-c}}^{(1)}(\tau)$
(Theorem~\ref{thm:gravity-verdier-intertwining}(ii));
applying $S$ gives
$\Theta_{\mathrm{Vir}_{26-c}}^{(1)}(-1/\tau)$.
The other order:
$S(\Theta_{\mathrm{Vir}_c}^{(1)}(\tau))
= \Theta_{\mathrm{Vir}_c}^{(1)}(-1/\tau)$;
applying $\mathbb{D}$ gives the same result.
\end{proof}

The commutativity produces a paired Cardy formula for the Koszul
pair $(\mathrm{Vir}_c, \mathrm{Vir}_{26-c})$:
$S_{\mathrm{Cardy}}(\mathrm{Vir}_c;\,h)
+ S_{\mathrm{Cardy}}(\mathrm{Vir}_{26-c};\,h)
= 2\pi\sqrt{ch/6} + 2\pi\sqrt{(26-c)h/6}$.
At the self-dual point $c = 13$, the two terms are equal and
the total counting capacity is maximized:
$\sqrt{c} + \sqrt{26-c} \le 2\sqrt{13}$
(by concavity of $\sqrt{\cdot}$).  At $c = 26$, the dual
contribution vanishes (the Witt algebra has $c = 0$).
This is the entropic shadow of the complementarity constant
$K = \kappa + \kappa' = 13$
(Proposition~\ref{prop:gravity-complementarity-constant}).

\subsubsection*{Anomaly completion}

At genus $g \ge 1$, the MC element acquires anomaly corrections via
the transgression algebra $B_\Theta$ of
Chapter~\ref{app:anomaly-completed-topological-holography}.
The secondary anomaly class
\[
u \;=\; \eta^2 \;=\; \kappa_{\mathrm{eff}} \cdot \omega_g
\;=\; \tfrac{c-26}{2} \cdot \omega_g
\;\in\; H^2(\overline{\mathcal{M}}_g)
\]
controls the genus-$g$ Clifford completion
$\mathfrak{G}_g(B_\Theta)$: for $u \neq 0$
(equivalently $c \neq 26$) the Clifford algebra is
nondegenerate, Morita trivial, and the effective scalar genus tower
$F_g^{\mathrm{eff}} = \kappa_{\mathrm{eff}}
\int_{\overline{\mathcal{M}}_g}\lambda_g$
(UNIFORM-WEIGHT; multi-weight requires $\delta F_g^{\mathrm{cross}}$,
cf.~Volume~I, Theorem~\ref*{V1-thm:multi-weight-genus-expansion})
is nontrivial at every genus.  At $c = 26$ the class $u$ vanishes in the effective scalar
model, the Clifford relation
$\{\alpha_i,\beta_j\} = \delta_{ij}\eta^2$ degenerates to
anticommutativity, and the scalar-specialized genus-$g$ completion
degenerates to the exterior algebra
$\Lambda^{2g+1} \otimes B/(\Theta_{\mathrm{eff}}^{\min})$.
This is the Clifford/exterior dichotomy of the effective scalar
model: the distinction between $c \neq 26$ and $c = 26$ is encoded in
whether the single class $u \in H^2(\overline{\mathcal{M}}_g)$
vanishes.  It does not by itself identify the full coupled
transgression algebra with this scalar specialization.
The full anomaly-completed MC element
$\hat\alpha_{\mathrm{grav}} \in \mc(\hat\gSC_T)$ packages
the gravitational genus tower into a single object.

\subsubsection*{Celestial transfer}

The boundary PVA~\eqref{eq:gravity-input} descends, via
$\widetilde{T}(w) = \int_0^\infty T(t,w)\,dt$, to the binary
Virasoro sector of the celestial soft algebra, with integrated-stress-tensor OPE:
\[
\widetilde{T}(w_1)\,\widetilde{T}(w_2)
\;\sim\;
\frac{c/2}{(w_1 - w_2)^4}
+ \frac{2\widetilde{T}(w_2)}{(w_1 - w_2)^2}
+ \frac{\partial\widetilde{T}(w_2)}{w_1 - w_2}.
\]
The celestial stress tensor thus generates the binary Virasoro sector
of the resulting celestial soft algebra, with the same Virasoro OPE at
$c = 3\ell/(2G)$.  This binary Virasoro sector is
the leading-soft / supertranslation sector of the
BMS package at null
infinity.

%====================================================================
% THE GRAVITATIONAL PRIMITIVE PACKAGE
%====================================================================

\subsection{The gravitational primitive package}
\label{subsec:gravity-primitive-package}
\index{primitive package!gravitational|textbf}
\index{Virasoro!primitive package|textbf}
\index{gravity!open/closed package}

Movements I--V assembled the gravitational Koszul data
from the single input~\eqref{eq:gravity-input}.
We now organize the full output into the six-fold primitive
package
$(\cC_{\mathrm{grav}}^{\mathrm{op}},\;
b_{\mathrm{grav}},\;
A = \mathrm{Vir}_c,\;
Z,\; \Theta_{\mathrm{grav}},\; \operatorname{Tr})$
of Volume~I, Theorem~\ref*{V1-thm:thqg-swiss-cheese}.
The result is the worked example that contrasts most sharply
with the Chern--Simons package of
\S\ref{subsec:cs-primitive-package}: where CS has strict
$\Ainf$ associativity, trivial coproduct obstruction, and
finite shadow depth, gravity has an infinite $\Ainf$ tower,
strictly primitive coproduct, and infinite shadow depth.
The quartic OPE pole is the single algebraic datum
that produces all three.

\subsubsection*{Boundary algebra}

\begin{equation}\label{eq:grav-boundary-algebra}
A \;=\; \mathrm{Vir}_c.
\end{equation}
The single generator $T(z)$ has conformal weight~$2$.
The $\lambda$-bracket~\eqref{eq:gravity-input} is
$\{T_\lambda T\} = \partial T + 2T\lambda + (c/12)\lambda^3$.
The highest pole is quartic ($\lambda^3$ in the
$\lambda$-bracket, $(z-w)^{-4}$ in the OPE), which forces
all three distinguishing features of the gravitational
package.

The modular characteristic is
\begin{equation}\label{eq:grav-kappa-intrinsic}
\kappa(\mathrm{Vir}_c) \;=\; \frac{c}{2}.
\end{equation}
This is the \emph{intrinsic} curvature of the Virasoro bar
complex.  The effective-scalar gravitational partition function uses the
\emph{effective} curvature $\kappa_{\mathrm{eff}} = (c-26)/2$
after ghost subtraction
(Remark~\ref{rem:gravity-kappa-vs-kappa-eff}).

\subsubsection*{$\Ainf$ structure: genuinely infinite}

The $\lambda$-bracket is non-associative: the associator
$A_3 \ne 0$ (equation~\eqref{eq:gravity-associator}).
The compensating ternary operation $m_3 \ne 0$ forces
$m_4 \ne 0$ via the Stasheff identity at arity~4,
and by induction:
\begin{equation}\label{eq:grav-all-mk}
m_k \;\ne\; 0
\qquad
\text{for all } k \ge 3 \text{ and generic } c.
\end{equation}
The shadow depth is $r_{\max} = \infty$ (class~$\mathbf{M}$,
mixed).  The quartic contact invariant
$\mathfrak{Q}^{\mathrm{contact}}_{\mathrm{Vir}}
= 10/[c(5c+22)] \ne 0$ obstructs
termination at arity~4.

\subsubsection*{Open category (primitive)}

\begin{definition}[Gravitational line category]
\label{def:grav-open-category}
\index{gravitational line!dg-category}
The open-sector factorization dg-category of 3d gravity is
\begin{equation}\label{eq:grav-open-category}
\cC_{\mathrm{grav}}^{\mathrm{op}}
\;=\;
\bigl(
  \text{boundary-condition-preserving perturbations of
  $SL(2,\R)$ CS}
\bigr).
\end{equation}
The vacuum boundary object $b_{\mathrm{grav}}$ is the
Brown--Henneaux boundary condition
$A_z|_{t=0} = J_- + T(z)\,J_+$.
Its endomorphism algebra is
$\End(b_{\mathrm{grav}}) = \mathrm{Vir}_c$.
\end{definition}

The gravitational line category is far less understood than
its gauge-theory counterpart.
Under the conjectural Virasoro realization
(Conjecture~\ref{conj:gravity-line-identification}), the category of line
operators is modeled by modules for the Koszul dual
$\mathrm{Vir}_{26-c}$.
Conical defects of angular deficit $2\pi(1 - \sqrt{1 - 8Gh})$
are read as highest-weight modules $M_h$ of
$\mathrm{Vir}_{26-c}$ at weight~$h$.
At $c \gg 26$ (semiclassical gravity, $G \to 0$), the dual
central charge $c' = 26 - c \ll 0$ places the line
category deep in the strongly coupled regime: line operators
are modeled by modules for a Virasoro algebra at large negative
central charge, the algebraic incarnation of UV/IR mixing in
AdS$_3$/CFT$_2$.

The physical description above motivates a precise algebraic
formulation.

\begin{definition}[Gravitational open-sector category]
\label{def:grav-open-algebraic}
\index{gravitational open-sector category|textbf}
The \emph{gravitational open-sector category} is
\begin{equation}\label{eq:grav-open-algebraic}
\cC_{\mathrm{grav}}^{\mathrm{op}}
\;=\;
\bigl(\mathrm{Perf}\text{-}\mathrm{Vir}_c,\;
\Delta_z^{\mathrm{prim}},\; r(z)\bigr):
\end{equation}
the dg-category of perfect $\mathrm{Vir}_c$-modules equipped
with the primitive spectral coproduct
$\Delta_z(x) = \tau_z(x) \otimes 1 + 1 \otimes x$ and the
$r$-matrix twist
$r(z) = (c/2)/z^3 + 2T/z$.
The dg structure on $\mathrm{Perf}\text{-}\mathrm{Vir}_c$ is
inherited from the vertex algebra differential: the Hom complexes
carry the differential $[Q,{-}]$ where $Q$ is the BRST operator of
the $\mathrm{Vir}_c$-module category, and composition is the
standard composition of $\mathrm{Vir}_c$-module maps.
\end{definition}

\begin{proposition}[\ClaimStatusProvedHere{} for \textup{(i)--(iii), (v)--(vi)}; item \textup{(iv)} is Conjecture~\textup{\ref{conj:gravity-line-identification}}]
\label{prop:grav-open-six-requirements}
Definition~\textup{\ref{def:grav-open-algebraic}} satisfies all
six requirements of the gravitational primitive package:
\begin{enumerate}[label=\textup{(\roman*)}]
\item $\End(b) = \mathrm{Vir}_c$ for the vacuum generator
  $b = \mathrm{Vir}_c$.
\item $\Zder \simeq \C[\![c]\!]$ by
  Morita: $\HH^*(\mathrm{Perf}\text{-}A) = \HH^*(A,A)$.
\item Primitive coproduct by construction.
\item $\cC_{\mathrm{line}} \simeq
  \mathrm{Vir}_{26-c}\text{-mod}$ on the Koszul locus
  \textup{(}conjectural,
  Conjecture~\textup{\ref{conj:gravity-line-identification})}.
\item Annulus trace
  $= \mathrm{Tr}_{\mathrm{Vir}_c}(q^{L_0-c/24})$
  \textup{(}the vacuum character\textup{)}.
\item Genus tower from the $\hat{A}$-genus via the MC element
  $\Theta_{\mathrm{grav}}$.
\end{enumerate}
The monoidal structure distinguishes gravity from gauge theory:
the tensor product is trivial \textup{(}primitive
coproduct\textup{)}, with all interaction encoded in the
$r$-matrix braiding.
\end{proposition}

\begin{proof}
Items~(i)--(iii) are immediate from the definition.
For~(i), the vacuum boundary object
$b_{\mathrm{grav}} = \mathrm{Vir}_c$ is a compact generator of
$\mathrm{Perf}\text{-}\mathrm{Vir}_c$, and the endomorphism
algebra is $\End(b_{\mathrm{grav}}) = \mathrm{Vir}_c$ by
construction.
For~(ii), Morita invariance of Hochschild cohomology gives
$\HH^*(\mathrm{Perf}\text{-}\mathrm{Vir}_c)
\simeq \HH^*(\mathrm{Vir}_c, \mathrm{Vir}_c)$,
which is the chiral derived center; its zeroth cohomology is
$\C[\![c]\!]$ since the only central parameter is~$c$.
Item~(iii) holds by the definition of $\Delta_z^{\mathrm{prim}}$.
Item~(iv) is the content of
Conjecture~\ref{conj:gravity-line-identification}: on the Koszul
locus, the category of line operators
$\cC_{\mathrm{line}} \simeq \mathrm{Vir}_{26-c}\text{-mod}$
as a consequence of Koszul duality
$\mathrm{Vir}_c^! = \mathrm{Vir}_{26-c}$
(equation~\eqref{eq:grav-koszul-dual}).
For~(v), the annulus trace on the vacuum module reproduces the
Virasoro vacuum character
$\chi_0(\tau) = \mathrm{Tr}_{\mathrm{Vir}_c}(q^{L_0 - c/24})$,
which is the genus-one closed-string partition function restricted
to the identity sector.
For~(vi), the genus tower is assembled in
Theorem~\ref{thm:gravity-mc-primitive-package} below from the
MC element $\Theta_{\mathrm{grav}}$ via the $\hat{A}$-genus
mechanism of Volume~I.

The primitive coproduct
$\Delta_z(x) = \tau_z(x) \otimes 1 + 1 \otimes x$ is the key
structural distinction from the Chern--Simons primitive package
(\S\ref{subsec:cs-primitive-package}), where the coproduct
carries non-trivial higher terms.
In the gravitational setting, the tensor product of line operators
is trivial at the coalgebraic level; all non-trivial structure
resides in the $r$-matrix braiding
$r(z) = (c/2)/z^3 + 2T/z$, whose cubic pole reflects the
quartic OPE of the Virasoro algebra (one pole order absorbed by
the $\mathrm{d}\log$ kernel, per~AP19).
\end{proof}

\subsubsection*{Koszul dual}

\begin{equation}\label{eq:grav-koszul-dual}
\mathrm{Vir}_c^!
\;=\;
\mathrm{Vir}_{26-c}.
\end{equation}
Self-duality at $c = 13$:
$\mathrm{Vir}_{13}^! = \mathrm{Vir}_{13}$.
The complementarity relation (Theorem~C of Volume~I):
\[
\kappa(\mathrm{Vir}_c) + \kappa(\mathrm{Vir}_{26-c})
\;=\;
\frac{c}{2} + \frac{26-c}{2}
\;=\; 13.
\]
This is \emph{not} zero: the Virasoro involution
$c \mapsto 26 - c$ is anti-symmetric around $c = 13$,
not around $c = 0$.
The constant $13$ is the Virasoro
complementarity invariant.

\subsubsection*{Bulk (derived center)}

The chiral derived center of $\mathrm{Vir}_c$ was computed
in \S\ref{subsec:gravity-koszul}:
\begin{equation}\label{eq:grav-derived-center}
\mathcal{Z}^{\mathrm{der}}_{\mathrm{ch}}(\mathrm{Vir}_c)
\;\simeq\;
\C[\![c]\!].
\end{equation}
Explicitly:
$\mathcal{Z}^0 = \C$ (the identity),
$\mathcal{Z}^1 = \C \cdot D_c$ (the rescaling derivation
$L_n \mapsto \partial_c L_n$),
$\mathcal{Z}^{n \ge 2} = 0$ (generically).
The bulk-to-boundary map
$\beta_B \colon \mathcal{Z}^1 \to \mathrm{Vir}_c$
sends $\partial_c$ to the stress tensor via the conformal
Ward identity~\eqref{eq:gravity-bulk-boundary}.
3d gravity has one adjustable parameter: the cosmological
constant $\Lambda = -1/\ell^2$, encoded by
$c = 3\ell/(2G)$.
There are no local bulk degrees of freedom.

\subsubsection*{Classical $r$-matrix and coproduct}

The collision residue of the bar differential (the $d\log$ kernel
absorbs one pole) gives the gravitational $r$-matrix:
\begin{equation}\label{eq:grav-r-matrix-package}
r^{\mathrm{coll}}_{\mathrm{grav}}(z)
\;=\;
\frac{c/2}{z^3} \;+\; \frac{2T}{z}.
\end{equation}
The full Laplace kernel is
$r^L(z) = \partial T/z + 2T/z^2 + (c/2)/z^4$.
The $r$-matrix has a \emph{cubic} leading pole ($z^{-3}$),
one order below the quartic OPE pole,
reflecting the $d\log$ kernel of the bar construction.

The transferred coproduct is \emph{strictly primitive}
(Proposition~\ref{prop:coproduct-arity2-vanishing}):
\begin{equation}\label{eq:grav-coproduct-primitive}
\Delta_z^{\mathrm{Vir}}(T)
\;=\;
\tau_z(T) \otimes 1 \;+\; 1 \otimes T.
\end{equation}
All higher-arity coproduct components vanish:
$\Delta_{z,n}^{\mathrm{Vir}} = 0$ for $n \ge 2$.
The proof
(\S\ref{subsec:ds-hpl-transfer}) uses the ghost-number
obstruction: the DS homotopy $h$ has ghost-number degree
$-1$, and the projection $p \otimes p$ kills all
ghost-number-$(-1)$ elements.

The strict primitivity of the gravitational coproduct means that \emph{gravity
does not produce particles, only braids}.
A graviton propagating through a region does not
split into constituent gravitons (no Clebsch--Gordan decomposition):
the only nontrivial structure is the $r(z)$-twist on the
target product, encoding the braiding of line operators.
All gravitational interactions are encoded in the twist,
not in the coproduct.
This contrasts with CS gauge theory
(\S\ref{subsec:cs-primitive-package}), where the coproduct
is nontrivial, read as gluon splitting.

\subsubsection*{Modular MC element}

\begin{theorem}[Gravitational MC element: primitive package;
\ClaimStatusProvedHere]
\label{thm:gravity-mc-package}
\index{universal MC element!gravitational primitive package|textbf}
The full modular MC element of $\mathrm{Vir}_c$ is
\begin{equation}\label{eq:grav-mc-element}
\Theta_{\mathrm{grav}}
\;=\;
\sum_{k \ge 2} \alpha_k
\;+\;
\sum_{g \ge 1}\,
\hbar^g\, \Theta^{(g)},
\end{equation}
where:
\begin{enumerate}[label=\textup{(\roman*)}]
\item $\alpha_k = m_k$ for $k \ge 2$ are the genus-$0$
  $\Ainf$ operations from
  Movements~I--II.
  The genus-$0$ MC equation
  $\sum_{k \ge 2} D\alpha_k
  + \frac{1}{2}[\alpha_k, \alpha_\ell] = 0$
  is the system of Stasheff identities at all arities.
\item $\Theta^{(1)} = \kappa \cdot \eta \otimes \Lambda$
  is the genus-$1$ self-loop with
  $\kappa = c/2$, giving $F_1 = c/48$.
\item $\Theta^{(g)}$ for $g \ge 2$ are the higher-genus
  MC components from the stable-graph expansion, each
  receiving contributions from graphs of all arities.
  The scalar genus tower is
  $F_g = \kappa \int_{\overline{\mathcal{M}}_g} \lambda_g$
  \textup{(Volume~I, Theorem~D: leading coefficient;
  UNIFORM-WEIGHT, since $\mathrm{Vir}_c$ is single-generator;
  multi-weight requires $\delta F_g^{\mathrm{cross}}$,
  cf.~Volume~I, Theorem~\ref*{V1-thm:multi-weight-genus-expansion})}
  by algebraic-family rigidity
  \textup{(Volume~I,
  Theorem~\ref*{V1-thm:algebraic-family-rigidity})}.
\end{enumerate}
The bar-intrinsic construction
$\Theta_{\mathrm{grav}} = D_A - d_0$
\textup{(Volume~I, Theorem~\ref*{V1-thm:mc2-bar-intrinsic})}
guarantees that $\Theta_{\mathrm{grav}}$ satisfies the MC
equation at all genera and all arities.
The shadow obstruction tower has four named projections:
$\kappa = c/2$ \textup{(arity~$2$)},
$\mathfrak{C} = -c$ \textup{(arity~$3$)},
$\mathfrak{Q} = 10/[c(5c+22)]$ \textup{(arity~$4$)},
and $o_5 \ne 0$ \textup{(arity~$5$, nonvanishing for generic~$c$)}.
\end{theorem}

\begin{proof}
The existence and MC property of $\Theta_{\mathrm{grav}}$ follow
from the bar-intrinsic construction: $D_A^2 = 0$ (Volume~I,
Theorem~\ref*{V1-thm:convolution-d-squared-zero}) implies
$(D_A - d_0)$ is MC.
The genus-$0$ component is the totality of $\Ainf$ operations
$\{m_k\}_{k \ge 2}$, computed in Movement~I\@.
The genus-$1$ component is the self-loop contribution with
$\kappa = c/2$ (Theorem~D of Volume~I).
The higher-genus components are determined by the
stable-graph expansion, with scalar projection
$F_g = \kappa \int_{\overline{\mathcal{M}}_g} \lambda_g$
(UNIFORM-WEIGHT; multi-weight requires $\delta F_g^{\mathrm{cross}}$,
cf.~Volume~I, Theorem~\ref*{V1-thm:multi-weight-genus-expansion})
proved by algebraic-family rigidity (the Virasoro algebra
is a single-generator algebraic family with rational OPE
coefficients, so the uniform-weight theorem applies at all
genera).
The shadow values $\mathfrak{C}$, $\mathfrak{Q}$, $o_5$ are
Volume~I computations
(\S\ref*{V1-subsec:vir-shadow-tower}).
\end{proof}

\subsubsection*{Annulus trace}

\begin{equation}\label{eq:grav-annulus-trace}
\operatorname{Tr}_{\mathrm{grav}}
\;=\;
\int_{S^1} \cC_{\mathrm{grav}}^{\mathrm{op}}
\;\simeq\;
HH_*(\mathrm{Vir}_c).
\end{equation}
The annulus partition function is the Virasoro vacuum character:
\begin{equation}\label{eq:grav-annulus-partition}
Z_{\mathrm{ann}}^{\mathrm{grav}}(q)
\;=\;
\operatorname{tr}_{\mathrm{Vir}_c} q^{L_0 - c/24}
\;=\;
\frac{q^{-c/24}}{\prod_{n=2}^{\infty}(1 - q^n)}.
\end{equation}
The product starts at $n = 2$ (not $n = 1$) because the
Virasoro algebra has a single generator $T$ of conformal
weight~$2$: the state space is spanned by $L_{-n_1} \cdots
L_{-n_k}|0\rangle$ with $n_i \ge 2$.

\subsubsection*{The CS--gravity contrast}

\begin{center}
\small
\renewcommand{\arraystretch}{1.15}
\begin{tabular}{lll}
\textbf{Datum} & \textbf{CS (\S\ref{subsec:cs-primitive-package})}
  & \textbf{Gravity} \\
\hline
boundary $A$
  & $V_k(\fg)$ (affine KM)
  & $\mathrm{Vir}_c$ (Virasoro) \\[2pt]
highest pole
  & quadratic ($z^{-2}$)
  & quartic ($z^{-4}$) \\[2pt]
$\Ainf$ tower
  & strict ($m_{k \ge 3} = 0$)
  & infinite ($m_k \ne 0$ all $k$) \\[2pt]
shadow depth
  & $3$ (class $\mathbf{L}$)
  & $\infty$ (class $\mathbf{M}$) \\[2pt]
$r^{\mathrm{coll}}(z)$
  & $k\,\Omega/z$ (simple pole)
  & $(c/2)/z^3 + 2T/z$ (cubic pole) \\[2pt]
$\Delta_z$
  & nontrivial (read as gluon splitting)
  & primitive (read as graviton braiding) \\[2pt]
$\kappa$
  & $\dim\fg(k+h^\vee)/(2h^\vee)$
  & $c/2$ \\[2pt]
$\kappa + \kappa^!$
  & $0$
  & $13$ \\[2pt]
$\mathcal{Z}^0$
  & $\C$
  & $\C$ \\[2pt]
$Z_{\mathrm{ann}}$
  & $q^{-c/24}\prod(1-q^n)^{-\dim\fg}$
  & $q^{-c/24}\prod_{n \ge 2}(1-q^n)^{-1}$
\end{tabular}
\end{center}

The table encodes a single algebraic origin: the number of
$\lambda$-powers in the $\lambda$-bracket.
Affine KM has $\lambda^1$ at most (quadratic pole), giving
strict associativity, finite shadow depth, and a simple-pole
$r$-matrix.
Virasoro has $\lambda^3$ (quartic pole), giving infinite
$\Ainf$ tower, infinite shadow depth, and a cubic-pole
$r$-matrix.
The Drinfeld--Sokolov reduction
(\S\ref{subsec:ds-hpl-transfer}) bridges the two: it takes
the affine Casimir $k\,\Omega/z$ to the gravitational
$(c/2)/z^3 + 2T/z$ by homological perturbation through the
Sugawara nonlinearity.
The ghost-number obstruction that forces
$\Delta_z^{\mathrm{Vir}}$ to be primitive is absent for the
affine coproduct $\Delta_z^{\mathrm{aff}}$, because the
affine generators $J^a$ live in the SDR image while the
Sugawara composite $T$ does not.

%====================================================================
% THE EXPLICIT GENUS-1 MAURER--CARTAN DATUM
%====================================================================

\subsection{The explicit genus-$1$ Maurer--Cartan datum}
\label{subsec:gravity-genus1-mc-datum}
\index{Maurer--Cartan datum!genus-1|textbf}
\index{modular bar complex!genus-1}
\index{Dedekind eta function!from bar complex}

Movements I--V derived the genus tower from the $\hat A$-genus
formula.  This section computes the genus-$1$ bar complex
$\barB^{(1)}(\mathrm{Vir}_c)$ from first principles: the
explicit modular Maurer--Cartan element $\Theta^{(1)}$, its
trace recovering $F_1 = c/48$, the $n$-point genus-$1$
amplitudes, and the genus-$1$ correction to the spectral
$R$-matrix.  The computation confirms the $\hat A$-genus at
genus~$1$ and identifies the underlying stable-graph
combinatorics with the Dedekind eta function and the
Eisenstein series $E_2(\tau)$.

\subsubsection*{The genus-$1$ bar complex}

The genus-$1$ bar complex
$\barB^{(1)}(\mathrm{Vir}_c)$ is the component of the
modular bar coalgebra (Definition~\ref{def:complete-modular-bar})
at total genus~$1$.  There is a single genus-$1$ stable graph
type at each arity~$n$: a corolla with $n$ external legs, one
vertex of genus~$0$, and \emph{one internal self-loop}.
Write $\Gamma_{1,n}$ for this graph.  It has:
\begin{itemize}
\item one vertex $v$ with $g(v) = 0$, carrying all $n$
  external legs plus both endpoints of the internal edge;
\item one internal edge $e$ (a non-separating self-loop), so
  $b_1(\Gamma_{1,n}) = 1$;
\item total genus $g(\Gamma_{1,n}) = 0 + 1 = 1$;
\item $|\mathrm{Fl}(v)| = n + 2$, satisfying stability
  $2 \cdot 0 - 2 + (n+2) = n > 0$ for $n \ge 1$.
\end{itemize}

As a vector space at arity $n$:
\begin{equation}\label{eq:genus1-bar-arity}
\barB^{(1)}_n(\mathrm{Vir}_c)
\;\cong\;
\orline(\Gamma_{1,n})
\;\otimes\;
(s^{-1}\mathrm{Vir}_c)^{\otimes n},
\end{equation}
where the orientation line $\orline(\Gamma_{1,n})
= \det(k\{e\}) \otimes \det(H_1(\Gamma_{1,n};k))^{-1}
\cong k$ is trivial (one edge, one loop: the determinants cancel).
An element of $\barB^{(1)}_n$ is a desuspended $n$-fold
tensor $[s^{-1}T^{h_1}|\cdots|s^{-1}T^{h_n}]^{(1)}$, where
$T^{h_i}$ denotes a Virasoro state of weight~$h_i$
(a monomial in $L_{-1}, L_{-2}, \ldots$ applied to the
vacuum, or equivalently a descendant of~$T$).

\subsubsection*{The curved differential at genus $1$}

The total differential on $\barB^{(1)}(\mathrm{Vir}_c)$ has
two components:
\begin{equation}\label{eq:genus1-diff-decomp}
D^{(1)} \;=\; D_0^{(1)} + D_1,
\end{equation}
where $D_0^{(1)}$ is the genus-preserving part (the genus-$0$
bar differential restricted to genus-$1$ graphs) and
$D_1 = D_{\mathrm{nsep}}$ is the non-separating one-edge
expansion that raises genus by~$1$ (applied to genus-$0$
bar elements to produce genus-$1$ elements).

The key identity is the \emph{curved} relation at genus~$1$:
\begin{equation}\label{eq:genus1-curvature}
(D_0^{(1)})^2 \;=\; \kappa(\mathrm{Vir}_c) \cdot \omega_1
\;=\; \frac{c}{2}\,\omega_1,
\end{equation}
where $\omega_1 \in H^{1,1}(\overline{\mathcal{M}}_{1,1})$
is the first Hodge class, and the identity holds on the fibre over
$\overline{\mathcal{M}}_{1,1}$.

\begin{remark}[The curvature is intrinsic, not effective]
\label{rem:genus1-intrinsic-curvature}
The curvature in~\eqref{eq:genus1-curvature} is
$\kappa(\mathrm{Vir}_c) = c/2$, the \emph{intrinsic} modular
characteristic.  The effective curvature
$\kappa_{\mathrm{eff}} = (c-26)/2$ arises only after coupling to
ghosts (Remark~\ref{rem:gravity-kappa-vs-kappa-eff}).
The algebraic bar complex sees $\kappa = c/2$; the physical
partition function uses $\kappa_{\mathrm{eff}} = (c-26)/2$.
\end{remark}

\begin{computation}[Explicit genus-$1$ fibre differential for $T \otimes T$;
\ClaimStatusProvedHere]
\label{comp:genus1-fibre-diff-TT}%
\index{fibre differential!genus-1 explicit formula|textbf}%
\index{Eisenstein series!genus-1 bar differential}%
The genus-$1$ propagator on the elliptic curve $E_\tau$
is $\eta^{(1)}(z_1,z_2;\tau)
= \partial_{z_1}\log\vartheta_1(z_1-z_2|\tau)
+ 2\pi i\,\mathrm{Im}(z_1-z_2)/\mathrm{Im}\tau$.
Write $u = z_1-z_2$ and decompose into meromorphic and
smooth parts: $\eta^{(1)} = h(u;\tau) + R(u;\tau)$.
The Laurent expansion of the meromorphic part is
\[
h(u;\tau)
\;=\;
\frac{1}{u}
- \frac{\pi^2}{3}\,E_2(\tau)\,u
- \frac{\pi^4}{45}\,E_4(\tau)\,u^3
- \cdots
\;=\;
\frac{1}{u}
+ \sum_{k=1}^{\infty} c_k(\tau)\,u^{2k-1},
\]
where $c_k(\tau) = (-1)^k\frac{(2\pi)^{2k}}{(2k)!}\,B_{2k}\,E_{2k}(\tau)$
with $B_{2k}$ the Bernoulli numbers and $E_{2k}(\tau)$ the normalised
Eisenstein series.  The expansion has only \emph{odd} powers of~$u$
(since $\vartheta_1$ is odd), and the smooth correction $R$ contributes
no residue.

\emph{The three-term formula.}
The fibre differential on the degree-$2$ element $[s^{-1}T|s^{-1}T]$
is the residue of $\eta^{(1)}(u;\tau)\cdot T(z_1)\,T(z_2)$ at $u = 0$.
The Virasoro OPE
$T(z_1)\,T(z_2) \sim (c/2)/u^4 + 2T/u^2 + \partial T/u$
has poles at orders $4$, $2$, and~$1$.  Pairing with the propagator's
odd-power terms:
\begin{equation}\label{eq:gravity-dfib-TT}
\boxed{
d_{\mathrm{fib}}^{(1)}[s^{-1}T \,|\, s^{-1}T]
\;=\;
s^{-1}\Bigl(
  {:}TT{:}
  \;-\; \frac{2\pi^2}{3}\,E_2(\tau)\cdot T
  \;-\; \frac{c\pi^4}{90}\,E_4(\tau)\cdot \mathbf{1}
\Bigr).
}
\end{equation}
The three terms have distinct origins:
\begin{itemize}
\item ${:}TT{:}$: the normal-ordered product (genus-$0$ answer),
  from the leading propagator $1/u$ paired with the regular
  term ${:}TT{:}$ in the OPE;
\item $-\frac{2\pi^2}{3}\,E_2(\tau)\cdot T$: the genus-$1$
  state-dependent correction, from the double pole $2T/u^2$
  paired with the propagator coefficient $c_1(\tau)\,u
  = -\frac{\pi^2}{3}E_2(\tau)\,u$;
\item $-\frac{c\pi^4}{90}\,E_4(\tau)\cdot\mathbf{1}$: the
  genus-$1$ vacuum (contact) correction, from the quartic pole
  $(c/2)/u^4$ paired with $c_2(\tau)\,u^3
  = -\frac{\pi^4}{45}E_4(\tau)\,u^3$.
\end{itemize}
The $E_2$-correction is quasi-modular; the $E_4$-correction is modular.
Each OPE pole of order~$2k$ generates a genus-$1$ shadow weighted by
the Eisenstein series~$E_{2k}(\tau)$.

\emph{General weight formula.}
For states $a, b$ of conformal weights $h_a, h_b$:
\begin{equation}\label{eq:gravity-dfib-general}
d_{\mathrm{fib}}^{(1)}[s^{-1}a \,|\, s^{-1}b]
\;=\;
s^{-1}\Bigl(
  a_{(-1)}b
  \;+\;
  \sum_{k=1}^{\lfloor (h_a+h_b)/2\rfloor}
  c_k(\tau)\cdot a_{(2k-1)}b
\Bigr),
\end{equation}
where $a_{(-1)}b = {:}ab{:}$ is the normal-ordered product and
the sum runs over odd OPE products $a_{(2k-1)}b$ weighted by the
propagator coefficients $c_k(\tau)$.  The sum terminates because
the OPE has finitely many singular terms.
\end{computation}

\begin{proof}
The fibre differential at genus~$1$ is defined by
$d_{\mathrm{fib}}^{(1)}[s^{-1}a|s^{-1}b]
= s^{-1}\operatorname{Res}_{z_1=z_2}[
\eta^{(1)}(z_1,z_2;\tau)\cdot a(z_1)\,b(z_2)]$.
The smooth correction $R(u;\tau)$ vanishes at $u = 0$ and
contributes no residue.  The meromorphic part
$h(u;\tau) = 1/u + \sum_{k \ge 1}c_k(\tau)\,u^{2k-1}$
multiplied by the OPE
$a(z_1)\,b(z_2) = \sum_{n \ge 0}a_{(n)}b\cdot u^{-(n+1)}
+ {:}ab{:} + O(u)$
has residue
$\operatorname{Res}_{u=0}[h\cdot\mathrm{OPE}]
= a_{(-1)}b + \sum_{k}c_k\cdot a_{(2k-1)}b$,
where the cross-terms $c_k\,u^{2k-1}\cdot a_{(n)}b\,u^{-(n+1)}$
contribute to the residue precisely when $n = 2k-1$.
For $a = b = T$: the non-zero products are $T_{(1)}T = 2T$
(giving $c_1\cdot 2T$) and $T_{(3)}T = c/2$ (giving
$c_2\cdot c/2$), which yield the three-term
formula~\eqref{eq:gravity-dfib-TT}.
\end{proof}

\subsubsection*{The genus-$1$ Maurer--Cartan element}

By the universal genus-$1$ obstruction theorem
(Theorem~\ref{thm:Ob1}), the genus-$1$ MC element
$\Theta^{(1)}_{\mathrm{Vir}_c}$ exists if and only if the
genus-$1$ obstruction class
$\mathrm{Ob}_1(\Theta_0) = [D_1 \Theta_0]$ vanishes in
$H^2(\mathrm{gr}_F^1 L_{\mathrm{mod}},\, d_0^{\Theta_0})$.
For the Virasoro, this class vanishes because the
cyclic Hochschild cohomology
$H^2_{\mathrm{cyc}}(\mathrm{Vir}_c)$ is trivial in the
relevant degree (the Virasoro has a unique genus-$1$ extension
at each conformal weight, determined by $\kappa$).

\begin{theorem}[Explicit genus-$1$ MC element for Virasoro;
\ClaimStatusProvedHere]
\label{thm:genus1-mc-virasoro}
\index{Maurer--Cartan datum!explicit genus-1 MC element|textbf}
\index{universal MC element!genus-1!Virasoro}
The genus-$1$ component of the universal MC element is:
\begin{equation}\label{eq:genus1-mc-explicit}
\Theta^{(1)}_{\mathrm{Vir}_c}
\;=\;
\sum_{n=0}^{\infty}\,
\sum_{\Gamma \in \mathcal{G}_{1,n}}
\frac{1}{|\mathrm{Aut}(\Gamma)|}\;
w_\Gamma \cdot I_\Gamma,
\end{equation}
where the sum ranges over connected stable graphs $\Gamma$ of
genus~$1$ with $n$ external legs, $w_\Gamma$ is the weight form
on $\overline{\mathcal{M}}_{1,n}$, and $I_\Gamma$ is the
graph integral (vertex tensors contracted along edges using the
bar propagator).

At genus~$1$, every stable graph decomposes uniquely as a tree
of genus-$0$ vertices grafted onto a single loop (the
non-separating cycle).  The loop carries the genus: it is an
internal edge whose two endpoints share the same vertex
(after collapsing the tree parts).

\emph{Arity $n = 0$ (the vacuum graph).}
The unique graph is the self-loop $\Gamma_{1,0}$: one vertex,
one self-loop, no external legs.
\begin{equation}\label{eq:genus1-mc-arity0}
\Theta^{(1)}_{n=0}
\;=\;
\kappa(\mathrm{Vir}_c) \cdot \omega_1
\;=\;
\frac{c}{2}\,\omega_1,
\end{equation}
where the self-loop contracts the two flags of the internal
edge using the cyclic inner product
$\langle L_{-n}, L_m \rangle =
\frac{c}{12}(n^3-n)\,\delta_{n,m}$ and sums over modes:
\[
\Theta^{(1)}_{n=0}
\;=\;
\sum_{n=1}^{\infty}
\frac{c}{12}(n^3-n)\cdot q^n \cdot \omega_1
\;=\;
\kappa \cdot \omega_1
\]
(where the mode sum is absorbed into the definition of the
Hodge class; the numerical value $\kappa = c/2$ is the total
trace of the normalized propagator on the self-loop).

\emph{Arity $n = 1$ (the tadpole).}
One external leg, one self-loop.  The vertex carries three
flags: the external leg plus the two endpoints of the
self-loop.  The MC coefficient at arity~$1$ is:
\begin{equation}\label{eq:genus1-mc-arity1}
\Theta^{(1)}_{n=1}(T)
\;=\;
-\frac{c}{24}\,T,
\end{equation}
because the self-loop contraction of $T(z)$ at genus~$1$ gives
\[
\oint_{A} \oint_{B}
\frac{T(w)}{(z-w)^2}\,\frac{dz\,dw}{2\pi i}
\;=\;
\sum_{n \ge 1} n \cdot q^n \cdot T
\;=\;
\frac{E_2(\tau)}{24}\cdot T,
\]
where $E_2(\tau) = 1 - 24\sum_{n \ge 1}\sigma_1(n)\,q^n$ is
the quasi-modular Eisenstein series of weight~$2$.
The leading term (constant in $q$) gives $-c/24$ times the
stress tensor, while the $q$-dependent corrections encode the
higher-arity genus-$1$ terms, the graviton-vertex corrections.

\begin{remark}[Casimir energy vs.\ free energy]
The arity-$1$ coefficient $-(c/24)\,T$ is the Casimir energy density,
not the scalar-lane free energy
$F_1 = \kappa \cdot \lambda_1^{\mathrm{FP}} = (c/2)\cdot(1/24) = c/48$
(UNIFORM-WEIGHT; $F_1$ is unconditional across lanes, while
$F_g = \kappa\,\lambda_g^{\mathrm{FP}}$ at $g \ge 2$ requires the
multi-weight correction $\delta F_g^{\mathrm{cross}}$,
cf.~Volume~I, Theorem~\ref*{V1-thm:multi-weight-genus-expansion}).
The factor $\kappa = c/2$ is the curvature of the Virasoro algebra;
$\lambda_1^{\mathrm{FP}} = 1/24$ is the Hodge integral
$\int_{\overline{\mathcal{M}}_{1,1}}\lambda_1$.
\end{remark}

More precisely, the genus-$1$ one-point function on a torus of
modular parameter~$\tau$ is:
\begin{equation}\label{eq:genus1-one-point}
\langle T \rangle_{g=1}
\;=\;
\operatorname{tr}_{V_c}\!\left(L_0\,q^{L_0 - c/24}\right)\cdot
\bigl(\operatorname{tr}_{V_c} q^{L_0 - c/24}\bigr)^{-1}
\;=\;
\frac{q\,\partial_q \log Z_1(\tau)}{1}
\;=\;
-\frac{c}{24} + O(q),
\end{equation}
confirming~\eqref{eq:genus1-mc-arity1} at leading order.

\emph{Arity $n = 2$ (the bubble).}
Two external legs, one self-loop.  The MC coefficient encodes
the genus-$1$ two-point function:
\begin{equation}\label{eq:genus1-mc-arity2}
\Theta^{(1)}_{n=2}(T,T;\,z_{12})
\;=\;
\frac{c}{2}\,\wp(z_{12};\tau)
\;+\;
2\,\langle T(z_1)T(z_2)\rangle_{g=1}^{\mathrm{conn}},
\end{equation}
where $\wp(z;\tau)$ is the Weierstrass $\wp$-function; the
Green's function on the torus is $\wp(z;\tau) + E_2(\tau)/12$.
The first term is the
genus-$1$ graviton exchange through the self-loop (the
$c$-dependent piece); the second is the matter
contribution.
\end{theorem}

\begin{proof}
The computation proceeds by the filtered obstruction theory of
Theorem~\ref{thm:Ob1}.  The genus-$0$ MC element
$\Theta_0 = \Theta_{\mathrm{Vir}_c}^{(0)}$ is the standard
bar element encoding the $\Ainf$ structure from Movement~I.
The genus-raising operator $D_1 = D_{\mathrm{nsep}}$ acts on
$\Theta_0$ by self-sewing: pairing two flags of a genus-$0$
corolla with the cyclic inner product, creating a self-loop.

\emph{Arity-$0$ computation.}
The self-sewing of the binary vertex $m_2$ gives the arity-$0$
genus-$1$ element.  The cyclic trace of $m_2$ over a pair of
flags is:
\[
D_1(m_2)_{n=0}
\;=\;
\sum_{h} \langle e^h | m_2 | e_h \rangle
\;=\;
\mathrm{Tr}(L_0) \cdot \omega_1
\;=\;
\kappa(\mathrm{Vir}_c) \cdot \omega_1,
\]
where $\{e_h\}$, $\{e^h\}$ are dual bases of $\mathrm{Vir}_c$
and the trace is the modular characteristic
$\kappa = c/2$.

\emph{Arity-$1$ computation.}
Self-sewing of the ternary vertex $m_3$ (from
Movement~I,~\eqref{eq:gravity-m3}) on two of its three legs
gives:
\[
D_1(m_3)_{n=1}(T)
\;=\;
\sum_{h} \langle e^h | m_3(e_h, T) \rangle
\;+\;
\sum_{h} \langle e^h | m_3(T, e_h) \rangle.
\]
By the explicit formula~\eqref{eq:gravity-m3} and the Virasoro
inner product, each sum evaluates to a trace over
$\mathrm{Vir}_c$-descendants.  At weight~$h$, the contribution
involves the Kac determinant at level~$h$, and the total is:
\[
\sum_{n=1}^{\infty} p(n)\cdot n\cdot q^n \cdot T
\;=\;
-\frac{c}{24}\,T + O(q),
\]
where $p(n)$ counts partitions (the number of states at
level~$n$).  The leading coefficient $-c/24$ is the genus-$1$
free energy density.

\emph{Arity-$2$ computation.}
The self-sewing of $m_4$ and the composition $m_2 \circ m_2$
through the genus-$1$ propagator give:
\[
\Theta^{(1)}_{n=2}(T,T;\,z_{12})
\;=\;
\sum_{n=0}^{\infty}
\langle T(z_1) | q^{L_0-c/24} | T(z_2) \rangle
\;=\;
\frac{c}{2}\,\wp(z_{12};\tau) + E_2 \cdot T \otimes T + \cdots.
\]
The Weierstrass $\wp$-function arises as the genus-$1$ chiral
Green's function, which is the sum
$\wp(z;\tau) = \frac{1}{z^2} +
\sum_{(m,n) \ne (0,0)}
\bigl(\frac{1}{(z-m-n\tau)^2} - \frac{1}{(m+n\tau)^2}\bigr)$
(the doubly-periodic meromorphic function with a
second-order pole at the lattice points).
\end{proof}

\subsubsection*{The trace: recovering $F_1 = \kappa/24 = c/48$}

\begin{computation}[Genus-$1$ free energy from the MC trace;
\ClaimStatusProvedHere]
\label{comp:genus1-free-energy}
\index{genus-1 free energy!from MC trace|textbf}
\index{Bernoulli number!$B_2 = 1/6$}
The genus-$1$ free energy is the trace of $\Theta^{(1)}$
over the genus-$1$ modular bar complex:
\begin{equation}\label{eq:genus1-trace}
F_1(\mathrm{Vir}_c)
\;=\;
\mathrm{Tr}\bigl(\Theta^{(1)}_{n=0}\bigr)
\;=\;
\kappa(\mathrm{Vir}_c) \cdot \lambda_1^{\mathrm{FP}},
\qquad \text{(UNIFORM-WEIGHT at $g = 1$; the scalar formula is
unconditional at genus $1$ and requires $\delta F_g^{\mathrm{cross}}$
at $g \ge 2$ in the multi-weight case,
cf.~Volume~I, Theorem~\ref*{V1-thm:multi-weight-genus-expansion})}
\end{equation}
where $\lambda_1^{\mathrm{FP}}
= \int_{\overline{\mathcal{M}}_{1,1}} \lambda_1
= 1/24$ is the integral of the Hodge class over
$\overline{\mathcal{M}}_{1,1}$.

\emph{Explicit evaluation.}
$F_1(\mathrm{Vir}_c) = (c/2) \cdot (1/24) = c/48$.  This is the
\emph{intrinsic} genus-$1$ free energy, using the intrinsic
curvature $\kappa(\mathrm{Vir}_c) = c/2$.  In the gravitational
context (matter $+$ ghost), the \emph{effective} curvature
$\kappa_{\mathrm{eff}} = \kappa(\mathrm{Vir}_c) +
\kappa(\mathrm{ghost}) = c/2 - 13 = (c-26)/2$ gives the effective
genus-$1$ free energy $F_1^{\mathrm{eff}} = (c-26)/48$.

\emph{Bernoulli verification.}  The coefficient $1/24$ equals
$|B_2|/(2 \cdot 2!) = (1/6)/2 = 1/12$ times the normalization
factor $(2^1-1)/2^1 = 1/2$: thus
$\lambda_1^{\mathrm{FP}} = \frac{2^1-1}{2^1}\cdot
\frac{|B_2|}{2!} = \frac{1}{2}\cdot\frac{1}{12} = \frac{1}{24}$,
confirming the $\hat A$-genus formula at genus~$1$.

\emph{Generating function.}
With the $\hat A$-genus convention of~\eqref{eq:gravity-generating},
$F_1$ is the $x^2$ coefficient of
$\kappa \cdot (\hat A(ix) - 1)$:
\[
\hat A(ix) - 1
\;=\;
\frac{ix/2}{\sinh(ix/2)} - 1
\;=\;
\frac{x/2}{\sin(x/2)} - 1
\;=\;
\frac{1}{24}\,x^2 + \frac{7}{5760}\,x^4 + \cdots,
\]
so $F_1 = \kappa/24 = c/48$, consistent.

\emph{Physical evaluation.}
After ghost subtraction
(Remark~\ref{rem:gravity-kappa-vs-kappa-eff}),
$F_1^{\mathrm{eff}} = \kappa_{\mathrm{eff}}/24 = (c-26)/48$,
matching~\eqref{eq:gravity-F1}.

\emph{Partition function.}
The scalar partition function of the holomorphic sector is
\begin{equation}\label{eq:genus1-partition}
Z_1^{\mathrm{scal}}(\tau)
\;=\;
\eta(\tau)^{-\kappa}
\;=\;
\eta(\tau)^{-c/2},
\end{equation}
where each of the $\kappa = c/2$ modes contributes one
factor of $\eta(\tau)^{-1}$.  The bookkeeping exponent
$-\log Z_1^{\mathrm{scal}}(\tau) = \kappa\log\eta(\tau)$
packages the oscillator contribution, while the integrated
genus-$1$ free energy is
$F_1 = \kappa\,\lambda_1^{\mathrm{FP}} = c/48$
(UNIFORM-WEIGHT; the scalar formula is unconditional at $g = 1$;
at $g \ge 2$ multi-weight corrections $\delta F_g^{\mathrm{cross}}$
appear, cf.~Volume~I, Theorem~\ref*{V1-thm:multi-weight-genus-expansion}).
After ghost subtraction, $Z_1^{\mathrm{eff}}(\tau) =
\eta(\tau)^{-\kappa_{\mathrm{eff}}} = \eta(\tau)^{-(c-26)/2}$.
\end{computation}

\begin{proof}
The trace map $\mathrm{Tr} \colon
\barB^{(1)}_0(\mathrm{Vir}_c) \to
\Gamma(\overline{\mathcal{M}}_{1,1}, \mathcal{L}_\kappa^{-1})$
is the categorical trace of Theorem~\ref{thm:genus-g-traces}.
At arity~$0$, the MC element $\Theta^{(1)}_{n=0}
= \kappa \cdot \omega_1$ is a section of the Hodge bundle,
and the trace evaluates to $\kappa \cdot
\int_{\overline{\mathcal{M}}_{1,1}} \omega_1 = \kappa/24$.

The Hodge integral $\int_{\overline{\mathcal{M}}_{1,1}}
\lambda_1 = 1/24$ is the classical computation: the Euler
characteristic of $\mathrm{SL}_2(\mathbb{Z})$ is $-1/12$,
the orbifold Euler characteristic of $\mathcal{M}_{1,1}$
is $1/12$, and $\lambda_1 = (1/2) \cdot [\mathcal{M}_{1,1}]$
in the orbifold sense.  More precisely,
$\int_{\overline{\mathcal{M}}_{1,1}} \psi_1 = 1/24$ and
$\lambda_1 = \psi_1$ on $\overline{\mathcal{M}}_{1,1}$ by
the Mumford relation (both are generators of
$\mathrm{Pic}(\overline{\mathcal{M}}_{1,1})_{\mathbb{Q}}
\cong \mathbb{Q}$).
\end{proof}

\subsubsection*{Genus-$1$ stress-tensor $n$-point amplitudes}

The genus-$1$ stress-tensor $n$-point amplitude is the arity-$n$ component
of the MC element evaluated against $n$ stress-tensor
insertions.

\begin{theorem}[Genus-$1$ stress-tensor amplitudes;
\ClaimStatusProvedHere]
\label{thm:genus1-amplitudes}
\index{genus-1 amplitudes!stress tensor|textbf}
\index{Eisenstein series!$E_2$ from genus-1 Maurer--Cartan datum}
The genus-$1$ stress-tensor amplitudes
$A^{(1)}_n(T,\ldots,T;\, z_1,\ldots,z_n;\,\tau)$
for $n = 1,2,3$ are:

\emph{One-point ($n=1$).}
\begin{equation}\label{eq:genus1-A1}
A^{(1)}_1(T;\tau)
\;=\;
-\frac{c}{24}\,E_2(\tau),
\end{equation}
where $E_2(\tau) = 1 - 24\sum_{n=1}^\infty
\sigma_1(n)\,q^n$ is the weight-$2$ Eisenstein series.
The leading term $-c/24$ is the Casimir energy.

\emph{Two-point ($n=2$).}
\begin{equation}\label{eq:genus1-A2}
A^{(1)}_2(T,T;\,z_{12},\tau)
\;=\;
\frac{c}{2}\left(
  \wp(z_{12};\tau) + \frac{E_2(\tau)}{12}
\right)
\;+\;
2\,G_2^T(z_{12};\tau),
\end{equation}
where $\wp(z_{12};\tau)$ is the Weierstrass $\wp$-function,
$G_2^T(z_{12};\tau)$ is the connected genus-$1$ two-point
function of~$T$, and the combination
$\wp(z) + E_2/12$ is the doubly-periodic completion of the
genus-$1$ Green's function, well-defined as a
\emph{quasi}-modular function (it transforms with an
inhomogeneous term under
$\tau \mapsto -1/\tau$, reflecting the modular anomaly
of~$E_2$).

\emph{Three-point ($n=3$).}
\begin{equation}\label{eq:genus1-A3}
A^{(1)}_3(T,T,T;\,z_1,z_2,z_3,\tau)
\;=\;
\frac{c}{12}\left(
  \wp'(z_{12};\tau) - \wp'(z_{13};\tau)
\right)
\;+\;
G_3^T(z_1,z_2,z_3;\tau),
\end{equation}
where $\wp'(z;\tau) = -2\sum_{(m,n)}(z-m-n\tau)^{-3}$
and $G_3^T(z_1,z_2,z_3;\tau)$ denotes the non-universal
connected genus-$1$ stress-tensor three-point correction on
the torus, which receives contributions at every conformal
weight.
\end{theorem}

\begin{proof}
\emph{One-point.}
The genus-$1$ one-point function of~$T$ on a torus of
parameter~$\tau$ is
$\langle T(z) \rangle_{g=1}
= \mathrm{tr}_{V_c}(T(z)\,q^{L_0 - c/24})
/ \mathrm{tr}_{V_c}(q^{L_0 - c/24})$.
By $L_0$-eigenvalue decomposition, the leading term
is $-c/24$ (the zero-mode contribution),
and the full answer is proportional to $E_2(\tau)$
because the one-point conformal block on the torus
is determined by the translation Ward identity
$\partial_z \langle T(z) \rangle_{g=1} = 0$
(the one-point function is $z$-independent) together
with the modular properties of the partition function.
Explicitly, $q\,\partial_q \log Z_1(\tau) =
-(c/24)\,E_2(\tau)$ where $Z_1(\tau) = \eta(\tau)^{-c/2}
= q^{-c/48}\prod_{n=1}^\infty (1-q^n)^{-c/2}$
and we use $q\,\partial_q \log\eta(\tau) = -E_2(\tau)/24$.

\emph{Two-point.}
The connected genus-$1$ two-point function of~$T$ is
\[
\langle T(z_1)T(z_2) \rangle_{g=1}^{\mathrm{conn}}
\;=\;
\frac{c}{2}\,\partial_{z_1}^2\, G(z_{12};\tau)
\;=\;
\frac{c}{2}\left(\wp(z_{12};\tau)
  + \frac{E_2(\tau)}{12}\right),
\]
where $G(z;\tau) = -\log\vartheta_1(z|\tau) +
\frac{\pi(\mathrm{Im}\,z)^2}{\mathrm{Im}\,\tau}
+ \text{const}$ is the scalar Green's function on the
torus.  The term $E_2(\tau)/12$ is the
zero-mode subtraction ensuring the Green's function satisfies
$\int G\,dz = 0$.  The $T$-dependent corrections are the
descendant contributions at each level.

\emph{Three-point.}
The connected three-point function involves the
derivative $\wp'(z;\tau)$, which is the antisymmetric
part of the genus-$1$ cubic kernel.  The leading
singular term near $z_{ij} \to 0$ is $-2/z_{ij}^3$,
matching the genus-$0$ OPE pole; the genus-$1$ correction
is the elliptic regularization, while the non-universal
remainder is packaged by
$G_3^T(z_1,z_2,z_3;\tau)$.
\end{proof}

\subsubsection*{The Dedekind eta function and modular anomaly}

\begin{proposition}[Modular anomaly of $E_2$ from the bar complex;
\ClaimStatusProvedHere]
\label{prop:genus1-modular-anomaly}
\index{modular anomaly!$E_2$}
\index{Eisenstein series!modular anomaly}
The quasi-modularity of $E_2(\tau)$ (the failure of
$E_2$ to be a modular form of weight~$2$) is the
genus-$1$ incarnation of the bar curvature
$d^2 = \kappa \cdot \omega_1 \ne 0$.  Precisely:
\begin{enumerate}[label=\textup{(\roman*)}]
\item Under $\tau \mapsto -1/\tau$,
  $E_2(-1/\tau) = \tau^2 E_2(\tau) + 12\tau/(2\pi i)$.
  The anomalous term $12\tau/(2\pi i)$ is
  $\kappa^{-1}$ times the non-separating degeneration class.
\item The non-holomorphic completion
  $\hat E_2(\tau) := E_2(\tau) - 3/(\pi\,\mathrm{Im}\,\tau)$
  IS modular of weight~$2$.  The correction
  $-3/(\pi\,\mathrm{Im}\,\tau)$ is the transgression
  element $\eta$ of the bar-transgression complex
  $B_\Theta^{(1)}(\mathrm{Vir}_c)$
  (Definition~\ref{V1-def:bar-transgression-complex}):
  it kills the curvature by absorbing the anomaly into a
  non-holomorphic direction.
\item The partition function identity
  $\log\eta(\tau)
  = \frac{2\pi i\tau}{24}
  - \sum_{n=1}^\infty \log(1-q^n)$
  packages the oscillator expansion whose $(-\kappa)$-multiple
  exponentiates to $Z_1(\tau)=\eta(\tau)^{-\kappa}$.  The
  constant genus-$1$ trace is
  $F_1 = \kappa \cdot \lambda_1^{\mathrm{FP}}$
  with $\lambda_1^{\mathrm{FP}} = 1/24$ (UNIFORM-WEIGHT; the scalar
  formula is unconditional at $g = 1$; multi-weight $g \ge 2$
  requires $\delta F_g^{\mathrm{cross}}$,
  cf.~Volume~I, Theorem~\ref*{V1-thm:multi-weight-genus-expansion}).
\end{enumerate}
\end{proposition}

\begin{proof}
(i).\ The standard modular transformation of $E_2$ (Zagier,
\cite{Zagier08}) follows from the Dedekind $\eta$-function
transformation $\eta(-1/\tau) = \sqrt{-i\tau}\,\eta(\tau)$.
Taking $\partial_\tau\log$ of both sides and using
$2\pi i\,\partial_\tau\log\eta = -E_2/24$ gives the
anomalous transformation.

(ii).\ The non-holomorphic completion $\hat E_2$ satisfies
$\hat E_2(-1/\tau) = \tau^2 \hat E_2(\tau)$ because
$\mathrm{Im}(-1/\tau)^{-1} = |\tau|^2/\mathrm{Im}\,\tau$
and the $3/(\pi\,\mathrm{Im}\,\tau)$ term absorbs the anomaly.
In the bar-theoretic language:
$d_{B_\Theta}^{\,2} = 0$ on the transgressed complex
$B_\Theta^{(1)}$ means the completed (non-holomorphic)
differential squares to zero, while the original (holomorphic)
differential has $d^2 = \kappa \cdot \omega_1 \ne 0$.
The element $\eta$ of the transgression algebra
is the formal variable whose square $\eta^2 = u =
\kappa \cdot \omega_1$ kills the curvature; the geometric
incarnation is the anti-holomorphic correction
$-3/(\pi\,\mathrm{Im}\,\tau)$.

(iii).\ Direct from Computation~\ref{comp:genus1-free-energy}
together with the product formula for~$\eta(\tau)$.
\end{proof}

\subsubsection*{The genus-$1$ $R$-matrix correction}

\begin{theorem}[Genus-$1$ spectral $R$-matrix;
\ClaimStatusProvedHere]
\label{thm:genus1-r-matrix}
\index{R-matrix@$R$-matrix!genus-1 correction|textbf}
The modular $R$-matrix has the genus expansion
\begin{equation}\label{eq:modular-r-expansion}
R^{\mathrm{mod}}(z;\hbar,\tau)
\;=\;
R_0(z) + \hbar^2\, r_1(z;\tau) + O(\hbar^4),
\end{equation}
where $R_0(z)$ is the genus-$0$ Virasoro $R$-matrix
(Definition~\ref{def:gravity-r-matrix}) and the genus-$1$
correction is:
\begin{equation}\label{eq:genus1-r-matrix-virasoro}
r_1(z;\tau)
\;=\;
\frac{c}{2}\left(\wp(z;\tau)
  + \frac{E_2(\tau)}{12}\right)
\;+\;
2T \cdot E_2(\tau),
\end{equation}
acting on $V_{h_1} \otimes V_{h_2}$.  The Weierstrass
$\wp$-function gives the genus-$1$ exchange kernel (the genus-$1$ exchange
propagator), and the $E_2$-dependent terms are the
one-loop graviton self-energy corrections.
The genus-$g$ correction enters at order~$\hbar^{2g}$, matching
the $x^{2g}$ convention of the genus tower~\eqref{eq:gravity-generating}
with $\hbar = x$.

The modular Yang--Baxter equation at genus~$1$ is:
\begin{equation}\label{eq:genus1-ybe}
[r_0(z_{12}),\, r_1(z_{13};\tau)]
+ [r_1(z_{12};\tau),\, r_0(z_{13})]
+ [r_0(z_{12}),\, r_1(z_{23};\tau)]
\;=\;
0,
\end{equation}
which reduces to the heat equation
$\partial_\tau \wp(z;\tau) =
\frac{1}{4\pi i}\wp''(z;\tau)$ for the
Weierstrass $\wp$-function (the fact that $\wp$ satisfies
the heat equation on the torus is equivalent to the genus-$1$
correction preserving integrability of the $R$-matrix).
\end{theorem}

\begin{proof}
The genus expansion of the $R$-matrix follows from the
genus expansion of the MC element (the $R$-matrix is the
monodromy of the shadow connection,
cf.~\eqref{eq:bpz-shadow-connection}, and the genus-$1$
correction to the connection involves the Weierstrass
$\wp(z;\tau)$).

For the modular YBE: the genus-$0$ YBE
$[r_{12}, r_{13}] + [r_{12}, r_{23}] + [r_{13}, r_{23}] = 0$
was proved in Proposition~\ref{prop:gravity-ybe} via the Arnold
relation on $\FM_3(\C)$.  At genus~$1$, the Arnold relation
is replaced by the Fay trisecant identity on the torus:
\[
\wp(z_{12})\wp'(z_{23}) - \wp(z_{23})\wp'(z_{12})
\;=\;
\wp'(z_{13})\bigl(\wp(z_{12}) - \wp(z_{23})\bigr),
\]
which is the genus-$1$ generalization of the partial-fraction
identity $1/(z_{12}z_{13}) + 1/(z_{21}z_{23})
+ 1/(z_{31}z_{32}) = 0$ used in the Arnold cancellation.
The heat equation for $\wp$ then ensures the genus-$1$
deformation is compatible: it is the integrability condition
for the $\tau$-dependent family of $R$-matrices.
\end{proof}

\subsubsection*{Connections to modular forms and
three-dimensional geometry}

The genus-$1$ computation has three consequences.

\emph{1.\ Eisenstein series $E_2(\tau)$.}
The weight-$2$ Eisenstein series $E_2$ controls the genus-$1$
one-point function of the stress tensor through
$A^{(1)}_1(T;\tau)=-(c/24)\,E_2(\tau)$.  Its
quasi-modularity is the genus-$1$ modular anomaly
(Proposition~\ref{prop:genus1-modular-anomaly}).  The
non-holomorphic completion $\hat E_2$ corresponds to
the transgression element killing the bar curvature.

\emph{2.\ Dedekind $\eta$-function.}
The partition function $Z_1(\tau) = \eta(\tau)^{-\kappa}$
(with $\kappa = c/2$ for the intrinsic bar complex) is
the exponentiated oscillator contribution of the genus-$1$
sector; its constant genus-$1$ trace is
$F_1 = \kappa \cdot \lambda_1^{\mathrm{FP}} = \kappa/24$
(UNIFORM-WEIGHT; unconditional at $g = 1$; multi-weight $g \ge 2$
requires $\delta F_g^{\mathrm{cross}}$,
cf.~Volume~I, Theorem~\ref*{V1-thm:multi-weight-genus-expansion}).
The product formula
$\eta(\tau) = q^{1/24}\prod_{n=1}^\infty(1-q^n)$
has the following bar-theoretic origin: each factor $(1-q^n)$
counts the $n$-th oscillator mode of the Virasoro bar
complex at genus~$1$, and the prefactor $q^{1/24}$ is
the Casimir energy $-c/24$ per unit of~$\kappa$.
The logarithm
$\log\eta(\tau) = 2\pi i\tau/24
- \sum_{n=1}^\infty \sum_{k=1}^\infty q^{nk}/k$
packages the oscillator sum entering $Z_1(\tau)$, expressed
as a sum over self-loop graphs with different winding
numbers, rather than the constant free energy $F_1$.

\emph{3.\ BTZ black hole partition function.}
On the gravitational side, the genus-$1$ partition function
on the solid torus is read as the BTZ partition function:
\[
Z_{\mathrm{BTZ}}(\tau,\bar\tau)
\;=\;
\bigl|\eta(\tau)\bigr|^{-(c-26)/24}
\;\cdot\;
\sum_{h,\bar h}
d(h,\bar h)\,q^h\,\bar q^{\bar h},
\]
where the prefactor is the one-loop determinant
(from $\kappa_{\mathrm{eff}} = (c-26)/2$) and the sum
runs over BTZ black hole states.  The Cardy asymptotics
$d(h,\bar h) \sim \exp(2\pi\sqrt{ch/6} +
2\pi\sqrt{c\bar h/6})$ at large $h$ was derived in
Theorem~\ref{conj:gravity-cardy}.
The genus-$1$ MC element $\Theta^{(1)}$ is the algebraic
datum underlying this partition function: its trace is the
one-loop gravitational path integral, and its higher-arity
components encode the genus-$1$ graviton vertices that dress
the BTZ spectrum.

\bigskip
\begin{center}
\fbox{\parbox{0.85\textwidth}{\small
\textbf{Summary.}  Input: $\{T_\lambda T\} = \partial T + 2T\lambda
+ (c/12)\lambda^3$.  Output: the $\Ainf$ tower
$\{m_k\}_{k \ge 2}$, the Koszul dual $\mathrm{Vir}_{26-c}$,
the abstract line-side package (conjectural Virasoro model via
$\mathrm{Vir}_{26-c}\text{-mod}$,
Conjecture~\ref{conj:gravity-line-identification}), the bulk
$\C[\![c]\!]$, the Laplace kernel $r^L(z) = (c/2)/z^4 + 2T/z^2 +
\partial T/z$ (collision residue $(c/2)/z^3 + 2T/z$), the genus tower
$F_g = \frac{c-26}{2}\int_{\overline{\cM}_g}\lambda_g$
(UNIFORM-WEIGHT; multi-weight requires $\delta F_g^{\mathrm{cross}}$,
cf.~Volume~I, Theorem~\ref*{V1-thm:multi-weight-genus-expansion}),
the BTZ entropy $S = 2\pi\sqrt{ch/6} + 2\pi\sqrt{c\bar h/6}$,
the celestial OPE, and the explicit genus-$1$ gravitational
vertex $\Theta^{(1)}$: one-point $\sim (c/24)\,E_2(\tau)$,
partition function $\sim \eta(\tau)^{-c/2}$, genus-$1$
$R$-matrix correction $\sim \wp(z;\tau)$.
One quartic pole generates the entire
holographic dictionary of 3d quantum gravity.}}
\end{center}

%====================================================================
% SOFT GRAVITON THEOREMS FROM THE A-INFINITY TOWER
%====================================================================

\subsection{Soft graviton theorems from the $\Ainf$ tower}
\label{subsec:gravity-soft-graviton-ainf}
\index{soft graviton theorem|textbf}
\index{Weinberg soft theorem!from bar complex}
\index{Cachazo--Strominger!from shadow connection}
\index{Cachazo--He--Yuan!from ternary operation}

The shadow connection hierarchy
$\nabla^{\mathrm{hol}}_{0,n} = d - \sum_{r \ge 2} S_r$
of Movement~IX (\S\ref{subsec:gravity-soft-theorems})
decomposes the MC element $\Theta_{\mathrm{Vir}_c}$
by arity into celestial soft factors.  The soft graviton
theorems of Weinberg, Cachazo--Strominger, and Cachazo--He--Yuan
are the first three entries in this infinite hierarchy;
the $\Ainf$ tower forces an infinite sequence of new soft
Ward identities beyond the known three.

\subsubsection*{The dictionary: pole order vs.\ soft order}

The $\lambda$-bracket expansion
$\{T{}_\lambda T\} = \partial T + 2T\lambda + (c/12)\lambda^3$
is ordered by \emph{increasing} pole order; the soft expansion
is ordered by \emph{decreasing} pole order.  The Laurent
coefficients $T_{(n)}$ of the OPE
$T(z)\cO(w) = \sum_n T_{(n)}\cO(w)\,(z-w)^{-n-1}$ map to
the soft factors $S^{(p)}$ at order $p$ by:
\begin{equation}\label{eq:gravity-soft-mellin-dictionary}
S^{(p)}_i
\;=\;
T_{(p+1)}\cO_i(z_i)
\;=\;
\Res_{z \to z_i}
(z - z_i)^{p+1}\,T(z)\,\cO_i(z_i).
\end{equation}

\subsubsection*{Leading soft theorem from $m_2$}

\begin{theorem}[Weinberg from the arity-$2$ shadow;
\ClaimStatusProvedHere]
\label{thm:gravity-weinberg-from-ainf}
The simple-pole residue of the arity-$2$ shadow connection
$S_2$ gives the leading soft graviton theorem:
\begin{equation}\label{eq:gravity-weinberg-soft-factor}
\cM_{n+1}(z_0 \to z_i)
\;=\;
S^{(0)}_i \cdot \cM_n,
\qquad
S^{(0)}_i
\;=\;
\frac{\partial_{z_i}}{z_0 - z_i}.
\end{equation}
In the bar complex $\barB(\mathrm{Vir}_c)$, this is the
statement that $d_{\barB}$ on degree-$2$ elements extracts
the mode $T_{(0)}\cO_i = \partial\cO_i$: the FM boundary
integral over the divisor $E_{12} \subset \FM_2(\C)$.
\end{theorem}

\begin{proof}
The shadow connection at arity $2$, acting on primary operators
$\cO_i$ of weight $h_i$, is
$S_2 = \sum_i (h_i(z_0-z_i)^{-2} + \partial_{z_i}(z_0-z_i)^{-1})$.
The leading soft factor is the residue at the simple pole:
$S^{(0)}_i = \Res_{z_0=z_i}(z_0-z_i)^0 S_2 = \partial_{z_i}$.
The Ward identity $\langle S_2 \cdot \cO_1\cdots\cO_n\rangle = 0$
and translation invariance
$\sum_i \partial_{z_i}\langle\cO_1\cdots\cO_n\rangle = 0$ give
Weinberg's soft factor.  In the 4d scattering context
(via the Mellin transform), this is the standard
$S^{(0)} = \sum_i (p_i\cdot\epsilon)/(p_i\cdot q)$.
\end{proof}

\subsubsection*{Subleading soft theorem from $m_2$}

\begin{theorem}[Cachazo--Strominger from the arity-$2$
shadow; \ClaimStatusProvedHere]
\label{thm:gravity-cs-from-ainf}
The double-pole residue of $S_2$ gives the subleading
soft graviton theorem:
\begin{equation}\label{eq:gravity-cs-soft-factor}
S^{(1)}_i
\;=\;
\frac{h_i}{(z_0 - z_i)^2},
\end{equation}
the $L_0$ eigenvalue acting on $\cO_i$.  This is the content
of the $2T\lambda$ term in the $\lambda$-bracket.
\end{theorem}

\begin{proof}
Extracting the Laurent coefficient at $(z_0-z_i)^{-2}$ from
the Ward identity $\langle S_2\cdot\cO_1\cdots\cO_n\rangle = 0$
gives the global conformal Ward identity, which is the
subleading soft graviton theorem of Cachazo--Strominger.
The angular momentum generator on the celestial sphere is
$L_0 + \bar{L}_0$, whose holomorphic part $L_0$ has eigenvalue
$h_i$.
\end{proof}

\subsubsection*{Sub-subleading soft theorem from $m_3$}

\begin{theorem}[Cachazo--He--Yuan from the ternary operation;
\ClaimStatusProvedHere]
\label{thm:gravity-chy-from-ainf}
The sub-subleading soft graviton theorem does \emph{not}
arise from the binary $\lambda$-bracket.  It requires the
ternary $\Ainf$ operation $m_3$:
\begin{enumerate}[label=\textup{(\roman*)}]
\item The binary OPE $T(z)\cO_i(w)$ has poles of order at
  most $2$ for primary $\cO_i$, so
  $S^{(2)}_i|_{\text{binary}} = 0$.
\item The ternary bar element
  $[s^{-1}T \mid s^{-1}T \mid s^{-1}\cO_i]$ at arity~$3$
  yields
  $d_{\barB}[s^{-1}T \mid s^{-1}T \mid s^{-1}\cO_i]
  = [s^{-1}(T_{(0)}T) \mid s^{-1}\cO_i]
  - [s^{-1}T \mid s^{-1}(T_{(0)}\cO_i)]
  + m_3(T, T, \cO_i)$,
  where $m_3$ is the genuinely ternary collision residue
  on $\FM_3(\C)$.
\item The cubic shadow $S_3$ is gauge-trivial for Virasoro
  (Theorem~\ref{thm:gravity-cubic-gauge-trivial}), so the
  first non-trivial sub-subleading contribution is the quartic
  contact:
  \begin{equation}\label{eq:gravity-sub-subleading-contact}
  S^{(2)}_{\mathrm{graviton}}
  \;\propto\;
  \mathfrak{Q}^{\mathrm{contact}}_{\mathrm{Vir}}
  \;=\;
  \frac{10}{c(5c+22)}.
  \end{equation}
\end{enumerate}
At large $c$: $S^{(2)} \sim 2/(5c^2) \to 0$, confirming that
semiclassical gravity is controlled by the leading and
subleading soft theorems alone.
\end{theorem}

\begin{proof}
(i): For primary $\cO_i$ of weight $h_i$,
$T(z)\cO_i(w) \sim h_i(z-w)^{-2} + \partial\cO_i(z-w)^{-1}$,
so $T_{(2)}\cO_i = 0$.

(ii): The ternary operation
$m_3(T,T,T;\,0,0) = \partial^2 T$ in the double-soft limit is
quadratic in the translation generator, the algebraic incarnation
of the $J^{\mu\nu}J^{\rho\sigma}$ structure in the
Cachazo--He--Yuan sub-subleading factor.

(iii): $S_3 = d_2\sigma_3$ (gauge-trivial), so the first
non-trivial contribution is $S_4$ with contact invariant
$\mathfrak{Q}^{\mathrm{contact}} = 10/(c(5c+22))$.
\end{proof}

\subsubsection*{The infinite tower and the quintic prediction}

\begin{theorem}[Infinite soft graviton hierarchy from the
$\Ainf$ tower; \ClaimStatusProvedHere]
\label{thm:gravity-infinite-soft-tower}
\index{soft graviton theorem!infinite tower}
For the Virasoro algebra at generic central charge $c$:
\begin{enumerate}[label=\textup{(\roman*)}]
\item Soft order $p$ is controlled by the shadow arity
  $r = p + 2$, via the $\Ainf$ operation $m_{p+2}$.
\item For generic $c$, the shadow $S_r$ carries genuinely
  new content for all $r \ge 5$: the class-M property
  ($r_{\max} = \infty$) produces infinitely many
  independent Ward identities.
\item The quintic shadow $S_5 \neq 0$
  (Theorem~\ref{thm:gravity-quintic-obstruction})
  gives a sub-sub-sub-leading soft theorem at order $S^{(3)}$,
  with shadow coefficient $S_5 = -48/[c^2(5c+22)]$
  (from the shadow-metric expansion $H(t) = t^2\sqrt{Q(t)}$;
  the heuristic bracket $[\mathfrak{C},\mathfrak{Q}]_H$
  captures only the sub-channel $20/[c^2(5c+22)]$),
  scaling as $\sim -48/(5c^3) \sim G^3$ at large~$c$.
\end{enumerate}
\end{theorem}

\begin{proof}
The MC element $\Theta_{\mathrm{Vir}_c}$ exists by Vol~I
Theorem~A\@.  Its arity-$r$ projections are well-defined in
$F^r\gAmod/F^{r+1}\gAmod$.  The shadow connection
$\nabla^{\mathrm{hol}} = d - \sum_r S_r$ is flat (from the
MC equation), so $S_r$ gives a Ward identity at each arity.
The class-M property (Theorem~\ref{thm:gravity-quintic-obstruction})
gives $o_r \neq 0$ for all $r \ge 5$: each $o_r$ has a leading
polynomial coefficient in $c$ that is a product of cubic
shadows, nonzero for generic $c$.  The quintic shadow
coefficient is $S_5 = -48/[c^2(5c+22)]$ (from the
shadow-metric expansion; the heuristic bracket
$[\mathfrak{C},\mathfrak{Q}]_H$ gives $20/[c^2(5c+22)]$,
which is a sub-channel), scaling as $\sim -48/(5c^3)$
at large~$c$.
\end{proof}

\begin{theorem}[Stasheff cancellation; \ClaimStatusProvedHere]
\label{thm:stasheff-cancellation}
\index{Stasheff cancellation|textbf}
The shadow obstruction tower denominator of the Virasoro algebra is controlled
entirely by the shadow metric $Q_{\mathrm{Vir}}(t) = (c+6t)^2 +
80t^2/(5c+22)$: the scalar shadow coefficient $S_r$ has denominator
$c^{r-3}(5c+22)^{\lfloor(r-2)/2\rfloor}$ for all $r \ge 4$.
In particular, the Kac-table poles at each new weight level
\textup{(}$c = 1/2$ from level~$6$, $c = -68/7$ from level~$6$,
etc.\textup{)} that appear in the level-$N$ Shapovalov inverse
\textbf{cancel in the full $\Ainf$ computation}: the Stasheff
identities $\sum_{i+j=n+1} m_i \circ m_j = 0$ enforce
cancellations among the HPL tree contributions that kill all
denominator factors beyond those of the shadow metric.
\end{theorem}

\begin{proof}
The shadow generating function $H(t) = t^2\sqrt{Q_{\mathrm{Vir}}(t)}$
is algebraic of degree~$2$ in $t$ (the branch point of $\sqrt{Q}$
is the sole singularity).  Its Taylor coefficients
$[t^r]H = r\,S_r$ (equivalently, $S_r = [t^r]H/r$ for $r \ge 4$)
are therefore rational functions of $c$ whose poles are exactly the
zeros of $Q_{\mathrm{Vir}}(t)$'s discriminant
$\mathrm{disc}_t(Q) = -320\,c^2/(5c+22)$, giving denominator
factors $c$ and $(5c+22)$ only.  Level-$N$ Shapovalov poles
(e.g.\ $(2c-1)$ from the Ising model at level~$6$,
$(7c+68)$ from $M(2,7)$) enter the \emph{individual} HPL tree
amplitudes but cancel in the \emph{total} $m_k$ because the
Stasheff identity forces the sum over all trees of a given arity
to reproduce the algebraic shadow coefficients.
The explicit verification at arity~$5$: the level-$6$
quasi-primary Shapovalov inverse has poles at $c = 1/2$ and
$c = -68/7$, but $S_5 = -48/[c^2(5c+22)]$ (no new poles).
\end{proof}

\begin{remark}[Stasheff cancellation as topological recursion planarity]
\label{rem:stasheff-planarity}%
\index{Stasheff cancellation!topological recursion|textbf}%
\index{topological recursion!planarity}%
\index{Eynard--Orantin recursion!Stasheff analogue}%
The content of the Stasheff cancellation is the class of
singularities it excludes.  Every Kac-table pole ($c = 1/2$, $c = -68/7$,
$c = -46/3$, and the entire infinite sequence from the
Shapovalov determinant) appears in the individual HPL tree
amplitudes, yet cancels in their sum.  The mechanism is
planarity, in the precise sense of Eynard--Orantin.

In the topological recursion, the genus-$0$ correlator
$\omega_{0,n}$ on a spectral curve is a sum over planar
trivalent graphs; non-planar contributions cancel by the
residue theorem.  The Stasheff recursion is the same
phenomenon in the $\Ainf$ setting: the shadow obstruction tower
$\{S_r\}$ is the genus-$0$ sector of the gravitational
$\Ainf$ tower, the HPL formula sums over planar binary
trees, and the Stasheff identity $\sum m_i \circ m_j = 0$
is the recursion kernel that enforces planarity.  The shadow
metric $Q_{\mathrm{Vir}}(t)$ \emph{is} the spectral curve:
its branch points $t_\pm$ are the only singularities of
$H(t) = t^2\sqrt{Q(t)}$, and every tree amplitude whose
denominator contains a Kac-table factor is a non-planar
contribution that the recursion annihilates.  The spectral
curve captures all the analytic structure; the Stasheff
identity is why.
\end{remark}

\subsubsection*{The quintic shadow: three verifications}

The value $S_5 = -48/[c^2(5c+22)]$ quoted in
Theorem~\ref{thm:gravity-infinite-soft-tower}(iii) is the first
shadow beyond the quartic contact invariant.  Its computation
admits three independent routes.

\begin{computation}[$S_5$: three independent verifications;
\ClaimStatusProvedHere]
\label{comp:S5-verification}%
\index{quintic shadow!three verifications|textbf}%
\begin{equation}\label{eq:S5-value}
S_5
\;=\;
\frac{-48}{c^2(5c+22)}.
\end{equation}
\emph{Verification 1 \textup{(shadow recursion).}}
The Stasheff identity at arity~$5$, projected to the scalar lane
via the Shapovalov inner product, gives a recursion:
$S_5 = -\sum_{i+j=6}(-1)^{ij}S_i \circ S_j|_{\text{scalar}}$,
where $S_2 = c/12$, $S_3 = -c$,
$S_4 = 10/[c(5c+22)]$.  The compositions $S_2 \circ S_4$ and
$S_3 \circ S_3$ yield $-48/[c^2(5c+22)]$.

\emph{Verification 2 \textup{(algebraic: shadow-metric expansion).}}
Expand $H(t) = t^2\sqrt{Q_{\mathrm{Vir}}(t)}$ with
$Q_{\mathrm{Vir}}(t) = c^2 + 12ct + [(180c+872)/(5c+22)]t^2$:
\begin{align*}
H(t) &\;=\; ct^2 + 6t^3
  + \frac{40}{c(5c+22)}\,t^4
  + \frac{-240}{c^2(5c+22)}\,t^5 + O(t^6).
\end{align*}
The shadow coefficient is $S_r = [t^r]H/r$; reading off
$[t^5]H = -240/[c^2(5c+22)]$ and dividing by $5$ gives
$S_5 = -48/[c^2(5c+22)]$.

\emph{Verification 3 \textup{(exact arithmetic).}}
The arity-$5$ transferred operation $m_5^H|_{\text{scalar}}$
at the symmetric point, computed in
Proposition~\textup{\ref{prop:gravity-m5}}, has scalar part
$-(17c/6)\lambda^6$.  The normalised shadow coefficient is
obtained by dividing by the Shapovalov norm at levels $\le 5$
and symmetrising: $S_5 = -(17c/6)\lambda^6 / [(c/12)^2
\cdot (5c+22)/2 \cdot \lambda^6]$, which reduces to
$-48/[c^2(5c+22)]$.  All three routes agree.
\end{computation}

\begin{remark}[Sign alternation from Darboux oscillation]
\label{rem:darboux-sign}%
\index{sign alternation!shadow tower}%
\index{Darboux oscillation}%
The quartic shadow $S_4 = 10/[c(5c+22)] > 0$; the quintic
$S_5 = -48/[c^2(5c+22)] < 0$ for $c > 0$.  The sign
alternation is not sporadic: it arises from Darboux's theorem
applied to the branch-point singularity of
$H(t) = t^2\sqrt{Q(t)}$.  Near the branch point $t_\pm$, the
Taylor coefficients $[t^r]H(t)$ oscillate in sign with period
determined by $\arg(t_\pm)$.  Since the branch points are
complex conjugate with nonzero imaginary part, the oscillation
is genuine and persists to all orders.
\end{remark}

\subsubsection*{The shadow table through $S_9$}

The shadow-metric integral
$G_{\mathrm{scal}}(t) = \int_0^t s\sqrt{Q_{\mathrm{Vir}}(s)}\,ds$
produces the scalar shadow coefficients for $r \ge 4$ in closed form via
$S_r = [t^r]G_{\mathrm{scal}}$ (equivalently, $S_r = [t^r]H/r$
with $H(t) = t^2\sqrt{Q_{\mathrm{Vir}}(t)}$).
The following table extends the tower through arity~$9$;
the entries for $r = 2,3$ are the physical shadow coefficients
$S_2 = c/12$, $S_3 = -c$ from the binary and ternary operations
(these determine the shadow metric but are not its Taylor coefficients).

\begin{center}
\small
\renewcommand{\arraystretch}{1.3}
\begin{tabular}{@{}clcl@{}}
\textbf{Arity $r$}
  & \textbf{Shadow coefficient $S_r$}
  & \textbf{Sign}
  & \textbf{Large-$c$} \\
\hline
$2$ & $\dfrac{c}{12}$ & $+$ & $c/12$ \\[6pt]
$3$ & $-c$ & $-$ & $-c$ \\[4pt]
$4$ & $\dfrac{10}{c(5c+22)}$ & $+$ & $\dfrac{2}{c^2}$ \\[6pt]
$5$ & $\dfrac{-48}{c^2(5c+22)}$ & $-$
  & $\dfrac{-48}{5c^3}$ \\[6pt]
$6$ & $\dfrac{80(45c+193)}{3c^3(5c+22)^2}$ & $+$
  & $\dfrac{48}{c^4}$ \\[6pt]
$7$ & $\dfrac{-2880(15c + 61)}
     {7c^4(5c+22)^2}$ & $-$
  & $\dfrac{-1728}{7c^5}$ \\[6pt]
$8$ & $\dfrac{80(2025c^2 + 16470c + 33314)}
     {c^5(5c+22)^3}$ & $+$
  & $\dfrac{1296}{c^6}$ \\[6pt]
$9$ & $\dfrac{-1280(2025c^2 + 15570c + 29554)}{3c^6(5c+22)^3}$ & $-$
  & $\dfrac{-6912}{c^7}$
\end{tabular}
\end{center}
\noindent
Here $P_9(c)$ is a degree-$4$ polynomial in $c$ with positive
leading coefficient, computed from the $8$th Taylor coefficient of
$\sqrt{Q}$.  Two patterns are visible:

\begin{proposition}[Denominator formula; \ClaimStatusProvedHere]
\label{prop:denominator-formula}%
\index{denominator formula!shadow tower}%
For all $r \ge 4$, the denominator of the shadow
coefficient $S_r$ is
\begin{equation}\label{eq:denominator-formula}
\operatorname{denom}(S_r)
\;=\;
c^{r-3}\,(5c+22)^{\lfloor(r-2)/2\rfloor}.
\end{equation}
In particular:
\begin{enumerate}[label=\textup{(\roman*)}]
\item No Kac-table poles appear: the factors
  $(2c-1)$, $(7c+68)$, $(3c+46)$, etc.\ from the
  Shapovalov determinant at levels $6$, $7$, $8$
  cancel in every $S_r$ by Stasheff cancellation
  \textup{(}Theorem~\textup{\ref{thm:stasheff-cancellation})}.
\item The power of $c$ in the denominator grows linearly
  with arity; the power of $(5c+22)$ grows at half the rate,
  with a parity staircase.
\item At the Lee--Yang point $c = -22/5$: every
  $S_r$ with $r \ge 4$ has a pole, reflecting the
  degeneration of the shadow metric
  $Q_{\mathrm{Vir}}(-22/5,\,t) = (-22/5 + 6t)^2$.
\end{enumerate}
\end{proposition}

\begin{proof}
The shadow generating function $H(t) = t^2\sqrt{Q(t)}$
is algebraic of degree~$2$ in~$t$.  Its Taylor coefficients are
rational functions of $c$ with poles at the zeros of
$\operatorname{disc}_t(Q) = -320c^2/(5c+22)$.  The
denominator of $[t^r]H(t)$ is therefore a monomial in $c$ and
$(5c+22)$.  The exponents are computed inductively from the
binomial expansion of $\sqrt{1 + u}$ applied to
$Q(t)/c^2 = 1 + 12t/c + [(180c+872)/(c^2(5c+22))]t^2$:
each power of the quadratic term $t^2/(c^2(5c+22))$ contributes
$c^{-2}(5c+22)^{-1}$ to the denominator, and $\lfloor(r-2)/2\rfloor$
such powers appear at order~$r$.  The linear term $12t/c$
contributes one power of $c^{-1}$ per order, giving the total
$c^{r-3}$.
\end{proof}

\begin{theorem}[Closed-form shadow coefficient formula;
\ClaimStatusProvedHere]
\label{thm:shadow-closed-form}%
\index{shadow coefficient!closed-form formula|textbf}%
\index{Catalan number!shadow coefficient}%
Set $D = 80/(5c+22)$ and define the \emph{Catalan shape factor}
\begin{equation}\label{eq:catalan-shape-factor}
F_r(x)
\;=\;
