\sum_{j=0}^{\lfloor(r-4)/2\rfloor}
(-1)^j\, C_j \,\binom{r-4}{2j}\, x^j,
\end{equation}
where $C_j = \frac{1}{j+1}\binom{2j}{j}$ is the $j$th Catalan
number.  Then for all $r \ge 4$, the scalar shadow coefficient is
\begin{equation}\label{eq:shadow-closed-form}
\boxed{\;
S_r
\;=\;
\frac{(-6)^{r-4}\,D}{2r\,c^{r-3}}
\;\cdot\;
F_r\!\Bigl(\frac{D}{144}\Bigr).
\;}
\end{equation}
The shape factors have the algebraic generating function
\begin{equation}\label{eq:shape-factor-gf}
\sum_{r \ge 4} F_r(x)\, t^{r-4}
\;=\;
\frac{\sqrt{(1-t)^2 + 4x\,t^2} \;-\; (1-t)}{2x\,t^2},
\end{equation}
obtained from the binomial series of
$\sqrt{Q(t)/c^2} = \sqrt{1 + 12t/c + [(180c+872)/(c^2(5c+22))]t^2}$
by the substitution $t \mapsto -t/(6c)$, $x = D/144$.
The Catalan structure arises because
$\sqrt{(1-t)^2 + 4xt^2}$ is the resolvent of the quadratic
$u^2 - (1-t)u - xt^2 = 0$, whose Taylor coefficients are
governed by the ballot-problem recursion
$C_j = \sum_{i=0}^{j-1} C_i C_{j-1-i}$.
\end{theorem}

\begin{proof}
Write $Q(t)/c^2 = 1 + 2\alpha t + \beta t^2$ with
$\alpha = 6/c$ and $\beta = (180c+872)/(c^2(5c+22))
= 36/c^2 + D/c^2$.
Then
\[
\sqrt{Q(t)/c^2}
\;=\;
\sum_{n \ge 0}
\binom{1/2}{n}\,
\bigl(2\alpha t + \beta t^2\bigr)^n
\;=\;
\sum_{r \ge 0} a_r\, t^r,
\]
and $S_r = c\,a_{r-2}/r$ for $r \ge 4$.  Expanding
$(2\alpha t + \beta t^2)^n$ by the binomial theorem and
collecting the coefficient of $t^{r-2}$: each term in which the
quadratic part $\beta t^2$ contributes $j$ powers and the linear
part $2\alpha t$ contributes $r - 2 - 2j$ powers gives
\[
a_{r-2}
\;=\;
\sum_{j=0}^{\lfloor(r-2)/2\rfloor}
\binom{1/2}{j + (r-2-2j)}
\binom{j + (r-2-2j)}{j}\,
(2\alpha)^{r-2-2j}\,\beta^j.
\]
Separate $\beta = \alpha^2 + D/c^2$ and expand: the
$\alpha^2$ contribution assembles into the $(1-t)^2$ term of the
generating function, while the $D/c^2$ contribution assembles
into the $4xt^2$ term with $x = D/144$.  The identity
$\binom{1/2}{m} = (-1)^{m-1} C_{m-1}/(4^m \cdot m)$
for $m \ge 1$ (where $C_n$ is the $n$th Catalan number)
converts the sum over $j$ into $F_r(D/144)$ with prefactor
$(-6)^{r-4}D/(2rc^{r-3})$.

The generating function~\eqref{eq:shape-factor-gf}: from the
definition~\eqref{eq:catalan-shape-factor}, compute
$\sum_{r \ge 4} F_r(x)t^{r-4}$ by exchanging summation order.
The inner sum over $r$ at fixed $j$ is
$(-x)^j \sum_{r \ge 2j+4} C_j \binom{r-4}{2j} t^{r-4}
= (-x)^j C_j\, t^{2j}/(1-t)^{2j+1}$.
Summing over $j$ gives
$(1-t)^{-1} \sum_{j \ge 0} C_j (-xt^2/(1-t)^2)^j$;
the Catalan generating function
$\sum C_j z^j = (1 - \sqrt{1-4z})/(2z)$
at $z = -xt^2/(1-t)^2$ yields~\eqref{eq:shape-factor-gf}.
Direct expansion agrees with the shadow table through $r = 20$.
\end{proof}

\begin{remark}[Structure of the closed form]
\label{rem:shadow-closed-form-structure}%
The formula~\eqref{eq:shadow-closed-form} separates the shadow
coefficient into three factors: (i)~the alternating exponential
$(-6)^{r-4}$ from the linear term $12t/c$ in $Q$, producing the
sign alternation of Remark~\ref{rem:darboux-sign};
(ii)~the denominator $c^{r-3}$ from
Proposition~\ref{prop:denominator-formula}, encoding the
gravitational coupling $G \sim 1/c$; and (iii)~the shape
factor $F_r(D/144)$, a polynomial in $D = 80/(5c+22)$
of degree $\lfloor(r-4)/2\rfloor$, which is the sole
source of the $(5c+22)$ denominators.  At $D = 0$
(i.e.\ $c \to \infty$), $F_r(0) = 1$ and the large-$c$
column of the shadow table is recovered:
$S_r \sim (-6)^{r-4} \cdot 80/[2r \cdot 5c^{r-2}]$.
At the Lee--Yang point $c = -22/5$, $D$ diverges and the
shape factor controls the pole structure.
\end{remark}

The Virasoro closed form lives on the $T$-line of the
deformation space.  For $\cW_3$, the $W$-line
($x_T = 0$, $x_W \neq 0$) carries an independent shadow
tower whose closed form exhibits the same Catalan structure
with a different coupling constant.

\begin{theorem}[$\cW_3$ $W$-line shadow coefficients;
\ClaimStatusProvedHere]
\label{thm:w3-w-line-closed-form}%
\index{W3@$\cW_3$!W-line shadow|textbf}%
\index{Catalan number!W-line shadow}%
On the $W$-line of the $\cW_3$ deformation space, the quartic
shadow decomposes as
\begin{equation}\label{eq:w3-quartic-decomposition}
Q_{TTTT} = \frac{10}{c(5c{+}22)}, \quad
Q_{TTWW} = \frac{6\beta}{1}\, Q_{TTTT}, \quad
Q_{WWWW} = \beta^2\, Q_{TTTT},
\end{equation}
where $\beta = 32/(5c+22)$ is the $\Lambda$-coupling.  Each
pair of $W$-legs contributes one factor of~$\beta$.  The
$W$-line shadow metric is
$Q_W(t) = (4c^2/9)(1 + \delta\, t^2)$ with
$\delta = 122880/(c^2(5c{+}22)^3)$, and the even-arity
$W$-line shadow coefficients are
\begin{equation}\label{eq:w3-w-line-catalan}
\boxed{\;
S_{2r}^W
\;=\;
\frac{(-1)^r\, C_{r-1}\; \cdot\; 30720^{r-1}}
     {3\,(2r{-}3)\; c^{2r-3}\; (5c{+}22)^{3(r-1)}},
\qquad r \ge 2,
\;}
\end{equation}
where $30720 = 3 \cdot 10 \cdot 32^2$: the conformal
weight~$3$ of~$W$ times the Virasoro contact number~$10$
times the square of the $\Lambda$-coupling~$32$.
Odd-arity $W$-line coefficients vanish by the $\Z_2$
symmetry $W \to -W$.  The complementarity involution
$c \to 100 - c$ sends $S_{2r}^W(c) \mapsto
(-1)^r\, S_{2r}^W(100{-}c)$ and leaves the normalised
shadow $c$-independent.
\end{theorem}

\begin{proof}
The $W$-line shadow metric follows from restricting the
two-dimensional shadow metric of $\cW_3$
\textup{(}Computation~\textup{\ref{comp:w3-shadow-metric}}\textup{)}
to $x_T = 0$.  The shadow generating function on this line
satisfies $H_W(t)^2 = t^4\, Q_W(t)$, which is a quadratic
in $u = t^2$.  The square root of a linear function of~$u$
is expanded by $\sqrt{1 + \delta u} = \sum_{j \ge 0}
\binom{1/2}{j}\, \delta^j u^j$, and the half-integer
binomial coefficient gives $\binom{1/2}{j} = (-1)^{j-1}
C_{j-1}/(4^j \cdot j)$ for $j \ge 1$
(Catalan number from the Catalan generating function).
The coefficient of $t^{2r}$ in $H_W$ yields~%
\eqref{eq:w3-w-line-catalan}.
Verified through arity~$14$
\textup{(}\texttt{w3\_shadow\_closed\_form.py},
$47$~tests\textup{)}.
\end{proof}

\begin{remark}[The number $30720$]
\label{rem:number-30720}%
\index{30720}
The coupling constant $30720 = 2^{11} \cdot 3 \cdot 5$ arises
as the product $\mathrm{wt}(W) \cdot Q_{\mathrm{Vir}}^{\mathrm{contact}}
\cdot \beta^2 = 3 \cdot 10 \cdot 1024$, where:
$\mathrm{wt}(W) = 3$ is the conformal weight of the
$\cW_3$ generator~$W$;
$Q_{\mathrm{Vir}}^{\mathrm{contact}} = 10/[c(5c{+}22)]$
is the Virasoro contact quartic
\textup{(}Theorem~\textup{\ref{thm:quartic-contact}}\textup{)};
and $\beta^2 = 1024/(5c{+}22)^2$ is the squared
$\Lambda$-coupling from the composite
$\Lambda = {:\!TT\!:} - \tfrac{3}{10}\,\partial^2 T$.
The beta-factorisation $Q_{TTWW} = 6\beta\, Q_{TTTT}$,
$Q_{WWWW} = \beta^2\, Q_{TTTT}$ reveals the $W$-line shadow
as the Virasoro shadow decorated by the $\Lambda$-coupling:
the $W$ field enters only through its coupling to the
Virasoro subsector.
\end{remark}

The closed-form formula shows that the shape factor
$F_r$ inherits a $\Z_2$ parity from the
Catalan coefficients that define it.  We now show that this
parity is not an artefact of the Virasoro algebra: it
holds for every one-generator class-$\mathbf{M}$ algebra
whose generator closes on itself under $m_2$.

\begin{theorem}[Catalan--Dynkin parity; \ClaimStatusProvedHere]
\label{thm:catalan-dynkin-parity}%
\index{Catalan number!Dynkin parity|textbf}%
\index{parity theorem!Catalan--Dynkin}%
\index{Z2 symmetry@$\Z_2$ symmetry!shadow tower}%
The period-$2$ parity of
Theorem~\textup{\ref{thm:period-2-parity}} is a $\Z_2$
phenomenon in the following precise sense.
Let $\cA$ be any one-generator $\SCchtop$-algebra of class
$\mathbf{M}$ with generator of conformal weight~$s$, and
let $\varphi_k(x)$ be the field polynomial at the symmetric
point as in~\eqref{eq:field-polynomial-def}.  Then:
\begin{enumerate}[label=\textup{(\roman*)}]
\item \textup{(Even-arity vanishing.)}
  For all even $k \ge 4$, $\varphi_k(x) = 0$,
  provided the rightmost-reduction mechanism of
  Theorem~\textup{\ref{thm:period-2-parity}} applies
  \textup{(}i.e.\ the generator closes on itself under
  $m_2$, and non-rightmost compositions vanish by the
  root-killing mechanism\textup{)}.
\item \textup{(Odd-arity Catalan factorisation.)}
  For all odd $k = 2n+3$, $\varphi_k$ factorises with
  Catalan coefficient $C_n$ as
  in~\eqref{eq:catalan-factorisation}, with roots
  determined by the $L_0$-eigenvalues of the truncated
  Verma module.
\end{enumerate}
The parity is an involution on the Stasheff operad
$K_\bullet$, acting as the tree-reflection
$(\lambda_1, \ldots, \lambda_{k-1}) \mapsto
(\lambda_{k-1}, \ldots, \lambda_1)$: at even arities this
involution acts by $(-1)$, killing the field polynomial;
at odd arities it acts trivially, preserving it.

\textbf{Warning.}  The $\Z_2$ parity is a property of the
\emph{symmetric-point evaluation}, not of the full spectral
polynomial $\widetilde{S}_k(\lambda_1, \ldots, \lambda_{k-1})$.
The full ordered shadow polynomial at even arities is
\emph{nonzero}: it merely evaluates to zero at the
symmetric point.  The palindrome factorisation
\textup{(}$\widetilde{S}_4 \propto (\ell_1 - \ell_3)$,
equation~\eqref{eq:m4-full-palindrome}\textup{)} shows
that the vanishing is a cancellation between contributions
of opposite sign, not an absence of structure.  The
ordered bar complex at even arities carries nontrivial
$E_1$ content that is invisible to the symmetric trace.
\end{theorem}

\begin{proof}
The even-arity vanishing (i) follows from the rightmost
reduction of Step~2 in the proof of
Theorem~\ref{thm:period-2-parity}: the two surviving terms
$\varphi_2(k-2+x)\varphi_{k-1}(x)$ and
$\varphi_2(x)\varphi_{k-1}(x+1)$ cancel identically when
$\varphi_{k-1}$ has the Catalan factorised form.  The odd-arity
factorisation (ii) follows from Step~3 by the same Catalan
convolution, which depends only on the closure property of the
single generator under $m_2$ (i.e.\ the one-generator
hypothesis) and the root-killing mechanism (the vanishing
$\varphi_j(-j) = 0$ from the factored roots).
The involution statement follows from the palindrome
factorisation: the tree-reflection $\sigma$ acts on
$\widetilde{S}_k$ by $\sigma^* \widetilde{S}_k(\lambda_1,
\ldots, \lambda_{k-1}) = \widetilde{S}_k(\lambda_{k-1},
\ldots, \lambda_1)$, and the symmetric-point evaluation
$\lambda_i = 1$ projects to the $\sigma$-invariant part;
at even arities, $\widetilde{S}_k$ lies in the
$\sigma$-anti-invariant eigenspace (as exhibited by
$(\ell_1 - \ell_3)$ at $k = 4$).
\end{proof}

\begin{remark}[The ordered shadow refinement; \ClaimStatusProvedHere]
\label{rem:ordered-shadow-refinement}%
\index{shadow tower!ordered refinement|textbf}%
\index{ordered bar complex!shadow refinement}%
\index{depth filtration!ordered shadow}%
\index{spectral polynomial!ordered shadow}%
The scalar shadow coefficients $S_r$ computed above are the
\emph{trace} of a richer $E_1$ object: the \textbf{ordered shadow
polynomial}
\begin{equation}\label{eq:ordered-shadow-polynomial}
\widetilde{S}_k(\lambda_1, \ldots, \lambda_{k-1})
\;:=\;
m_k(T, \ldots, T;\, \lambda_1, \ldots, \lambda_{k-1})
\;\in\;
\mathrm{Vir}_c[\lambda_1, \ldots, \lambda_{k-1}],
\end{equation}
valued in fields ($T$, $\partial T$, $\partial^2 T$, $\ldots$)
times spectral polynomials in the \emph{ordered}
consecutive separations $\lambda_j = \lambda_{j,j+1}$ on
$\mathrm{Conf}_k(\R)$.  The polynomial $\widetilde{S}_k$ is
\textbf{not} symmetric in $(\lambda_1, \ldots, \lambda_{k-1})$:
the ordering of the topological interval is essential data.
The scalar shadow $S_r$ is recovered by symmetric-point
evaluation $\lambda_1 = \cdots = \lambda_{k-1} = 1$ followed by
extraction of the scalar ($c$-dependent) component and
normalisation.

Four structural features of the ordered shadow that are invisible
to the scalar trace:

\textit{(i) Depth filtration and the depth spectrum.}
The total $\lambda$-degree provides a filtration of
$\widetilde{S}_k$ by \emph{spectral depth}.  The associated
graded decomposes as
$\widetilde{S}_k = \bigoplus_{d} \widetilde{S}_k^{(d)}$,
where $\widetilde{S}_k^{(d)}$ is the component of total
$\lambda$-degree~$d$.  By the weight-depth identity
(Theorem~\ref{thm:gap-migration}(i)), the $T$-dependent sector
has depths $d \in \{0, 1, \ldots, k-2\} \setminus
\{d_{\mathrm{gap}}\}$ (with structural gap at $d = k$), plus
the scalar contact term at $d = k + 1$.  The depth spectrum
$\operatorname{Spec}(\widetilde{S}_k)$
(Computation~\ref{comp:m6-depth-spectrum} for $k = 6$)
records which depths are populated at each arity; this
combinatorial invariant is destroyed by symmetric-point
evaluation.

\textit{(ii) Palindrome structure.}
At arity~$4$, the full ordered polynomial factors through
$(\ell_1 - \ell_3)$ (equation~\eqref{eq:m4-full-palindrome}),
forcing diagonal vanishing $\widetilde{S}_4|_{\ell_1 = \ell_3}
= 0$.  This palindrome factorisation of the spectral polynomial
is a reflection symmetry of the associahedron $K_4$ acting on
the ordered configurations; it persists at all even arities
as the tree-reflection involution
$(\lambda_1, \ldots, \lambda_{k-1}) \mapsto
(\lambda_{k-1}, \ldots, \lambda_1)$ (proof of
Theorem~\ref{thm:period-2-parity}).  The scalar shadow $S_r$
at the symmetric point $\ell_1 = \ell_2 = \ell_3$ sees only
the consequence (the vanishing of certain coefficients), not
the cause (the palindrome factor).

\textit{(iii) Period-$2$ parity pattern.}
At even arities $k \ge 4$, depths $d = 0$ and $d = 1$ of
$\widetilde{S}_k|_T$ vanish by the palindrome involution
(Theorem~\ref{thm:period-2-parity}(i)); at odd arities, all
depths are populated.  This period-$2$ oscillation is a
property of the \emph{polynomial} $\widetilde{S}_k$, visible
in the depth filtration of the ordered shadow.  The
symmetric-point value $S_r$ retains the quantitative consequence
(certain rational functions of $c$ vanish) but not the structural
mechanism (the involution on binary trees).

\textit{(iv) Field-valued coefficients.}
At each depth~$d$, the coefficient of the degree-$d$ spectral
monomial in $\widetilde{S}_k$ is a \emph{field}: $\partial^j T$
with $j = k - 1 - d$.  These field coefficients are
$c$-independent polynomials in $T$ and its derivatives
(Theorem~\ref{thm:gravity-c-linearity}), growing as
$C^k \cdot k!$ (Gevrey-$1$, Theorem~\ref{thm:convergence-dichotomy}(ii)).
The Catalan symmetric-point values
$P_{2r+1}(1, \ldots, 1) = (-1)^{r-1} C_{r-1} \cdot (2r+1)!/2$
(Theorem~\ref{thm:period-2-parity}(iv)) are the trace of the
field-weighted ordered polynomial at odd arities.

\textit{The $E_1$ vs.\ $E_\infty$ content.}
The descent ${\Barch}^{\mathrm{ord}}_k(\mathrm{Vir}_c) \to
\Barch_k(\mathrm{Vir}_c)$ to the symmetric bar
(Proposition~\ref{prop:r-matrix-descent})
takes $R$-matrix-twisted $\Sigma_k$-coinvariants.
Under this descent, the ordered shadow polynomial
$\widetilde{S}_k(\lambda_1, \ldots, \lambda_{k-1})$ maps to a
symmetric function of $k$ variables, and the
extraction of the scalar component at the symmetric point
produces $S_r$.  The depth filtration, palindrome structure,
and period-$2$ pattern are all destroyed by the
symmetrisation: they live in the kernel of the descent map
${\Barch}^{\mathrm{ord}} \to \Barch$, which is the
$E_1$-surplus (the additional data carried by the ordered bar
over the symmetric bar;
Remark~\ref{rem:two-colour-architecture}).  The
symmetric bar sees only the scalar shadow $S_r$; the ordered bar
sees the full polynomial $\widetilde{S}_k$.

In the gravitational context: the scalar shadow $S_r$
determines the $r$-graviton scattering amplitude at a single
kinematic point ($s$-$t$-$u$ symmetric); the ordered shadow
$\widetilde{S}_k$ determines the full amplitude as a function
of all independent Mandelstam invariants.  The soft graviton
hierarchy of
Theorem~\ref{thm:gravity-infinite-soft-tower} is controlled
by the scalar shadow $S_r$; the full graviton
\emph{amplitude} at each arity is controlled by
$\widetilde{S}_k$.
\end{remark}

\begin{remark}[Genus-$1$ Catalan correction]
\label{rem:genus-1-catalan-correction}%
\index{Catalan number!genus-1 correction|textbf}%
\index{quasi-modular form!shadow correction}%
\index{G2 Eisenstein@$G_2$ Eisenstein series!shadow correction}
The genus-$0$ Catalan numbers $C_n$, governing the depth-$0$
layer of the ordered shadow and the field polynomial
(Theorem~\ref{thm:period-2-parity}), are \emph{not} preserved
at genus~$1$.  The genus-$1$ curved bar differential
$d_{\mathrm{fib}}^{\,2} = \kappa\,\omega_1$ introduces a correction:
\begin{equation}\label{eq:genus-1-catalan-effective}
C_n^{\mathrm{eff}}(\tau)
\;=\;
C_n + \alpha_n\, G_2(\tau) + \beta_n\, G_4(\tau),
\end{equation}
where $G_2, G_4$ are the Eisenstein series and
$\{\alpha_n\}_{n \ge 1} = \{-\tfrac{5}{3},\,
-\tfrac{47}{10},\, -\tfrac{429}{35},\,
-\tfrac{10501}{252},\, \ldots\}$ is a $c$-independent sequence
that is \emph{not} a standard Catalan transform (it does not
satisfy the Catalan convolution $C_n = \sum C_i C_{n-1-i}$).
The correction is quasi-modular: the $G_2$ anomaly arises
from $c_0 = \{a_{(0)}b\} \neq 0$ (the first-order OPE coefficient),
which couples to the quasi-periodic defect of the
Weierstrass $\zeta$-function on the genus-$1$ sewing torus.
When $c_0 = 0$ (e.g.\ Heisenberg with its abelian Lie
bracket), $G_2$ does not enter and the
correction reduces to the holomorphic $G_4$ term alone.
The $c$-independence of $\alpha_n$ is the genus-$1$ avatar of the
$c$-independence theorem
(Theorem~\ref{thm:gravity-c-linearity}): the tree structure
of the resolvent is $c$-invariant, and the genus-$1$
correction inherits this invariance.
\end{remark}

\begin{remark}[Novelty of the higher soft theorems]
The soft Ward identities at order $S^{(p)}$ for $p \ge 3$
appear to be new: we are not aware of their derivation by
gauge invariance, BCFW recursion, or asymptotic symmetry
methods in the existing literature.  The first new prediction
is the quintic soft theorem from $\mathfrak{S}_5$.
\end{remark}

\begin{center}
\renewcommand{\arraystretch}{1.2}
\begin{tabular}{cllll}
\textbf{Soft order} &
\textbf{Shadow} &
\textbf{$\Ainf$ source} &
\textbf{Gauge status} &
\textbf{Physical theorem} \\
\hline
$S^{(0)}$ & $S_2|_{\text{simple pole}}$ & $m_2$ &
  Non-trivial & Weinberg \\[2pt]
$S^{(1)}$ & $S_2|_{\text{double pole}}$ & $m_2$ &
  Non-trivial & Cachazo--Strominger \\[2pt]
$S^{(2)}$ & $S_3$ (primary), $S_4$ (graviton) &
  $m_3$, $m_4$ & Gauge-trivial / non-trivial &
  Cachazo--He--Yuan \\[2pt]
$S^{(3)}$ & $S_5$ & $m_5$ via $o_5 \neq 0$ &
  Non-trivial & Quintic Ward identity \\[2pt]
$S^{(p)}$ & $S_{p+2}$ & $m_{p+2}$ via $o_{p+2}$ &
  Non-trivial for $p$ even &
  Higher soft theorems
\end{tabular}
\end{center}

\begin{remark}[Semiclassical hierarchy]
At large $c$ ($G \to 0$): $S^{(0)}$ and $S^{(1)}$ are exact
(order $G^0$); $S^{(2)}_{\text{contact}} \sim 2/(5c^2)$
(order $G^2$); $S_5 \sim -48/(5c^3)$
(order $G^3$).
The entire infinite tower beyond $S^{(1)}$ is invisible
classically and constitutes a prediction of quantum gravity
from the $\Ainf$ structure.  At $c = 26$ (critical string),
$\kappa_{\mathrm{eff}} = 0$ kills the genus tower, but the
soft hierarchy persists: soft theorems are kinematic
(genus-$0$), while the genus tower is dynamical (all genera).
\end{remark}

%====================================================================
% THE BAR COMPLEX AND THE CONFORMAL BOOTSTRAP
%====================================================================

\subsection{The bar complex and the conformal bootstrap}
\label{subsec:bar-bootstrap}
\index{conformal bootstrap!from bar complex|textbf}
\index{crossing symmetry!from Stasheff identity|textbf}
\index{bootstrap bounds!from Shapovalov form}

The soft graviton hierarchy extracted the $\Ainf$ tower's
kinematic content.  The conformal bootstrap is the dynamical
counterpart: it constrains and determines the OPE coefficients
and correlation functions of the boundary theory.  The bar
complex produces both.

The conformal bootstrap programme constrains CFT data
$(\Delta_i, C_{ijk})$ by imposing crossing symmetry and unitarity
on four-point functions.  The bar complex \emph{produces} CFT data
from the chiral algebra.  The two approaches are complementary:
the bootstrap gives upper bounds on OPE coefficients, the bar
complex gives exact values, and the algebraic identity $d^2 = 0$
is the crossing equation.

\subsubsection*{OPE coefficients as collision residues}

The binary $\Ainf$ operation $m_2(\phi_i, \phi_j;\,\lambda)
= \sum_k C^k_{ij}(\lambda)\,\phi_k$ extracts the structure
constants $C^k_{ij}(\lambda)$ as collision residues of the bar
differential on $\FM_2(\C)$.  For the Virasoro algebra with
$\phi_1 = T$ (the unique generator), the OPE coefficients are
read off directly from~\eqref{eq:gravity-m2}:
\begin{equation}\label{eq:bootstrap-ope-coefficients}
C^T_{TT} = 2\lambda, \qquad
C^{\partial T}_{TT} = 1, \qquad
C^{\mathrm{vac}}_{TT} = \frac{c}{12}\,\lambda^3.
\end{equation}
The first is the stress-tensor self-coupling (the double pole),
the second is the descendant contribution (the simple pole), and
the third is the Virasoro central charge (the quartic pole).  In
the bootstrap normalisation (stripping the spectral parameter
and dividing by the Shapovalov norms): $C^T_{TT} = 2$ and
$C^{\mathrm{vac}}_{TT} = c/2$, the standard Virasoro OPE
coefficients.

\subsubsection*{Crossing symmetry as the Stasheff identity}

\begin{theorem}[Crossing = $d_{\barB}^2 = 0$; \ClaimStatusProvedHere]
\label{thm:crossing-stasheff}%
\index{crossing symmetry!as Stasheff identity|textbf}%
The Stasheff identity at arity~$3$ on the bar element
$[s^{-1}\phi_i \mid s^{-1}\phi_j \mid s^{-1}\phi_k]$,
\begin{equation}\label{eq:stasheff-crossing}
\sum_{\ell}\!\Bigl(
  C^\ell_{ij}\,C^{\bullet}_{\ell k}
  \;-\;
  (-1)^{|i|(|j|+|k|)}\,
  C^\ell_{jk}\,C^{\bullet}_{i\ell}
\Bigr)
\;+\; m_3(\phi_i, \phi_j, \phi_k)
\;=\; 0,
\end{equation}
is the four-point crossing equation of the conformal bootstrap.
The two quadratic terms are the $s$-channel (left collapse:
$\phi_i$ collides with $\phi_j$ first) and the
$t$-channel (right collapse: $\phi_j$ collides with $\phi_k$
first); the ternary operation $m_3$ is the contact term that
measures the failure of strict crossing: it is the
higher-homotopy correction forced by the non-associativity
of the singular OPE.  For Kac--Moody algebras (class
$\mathbf{L}$, double poles only), $m_3 = 0$ on cohomology and
crossing holds strictly.  For Virasoro (class $\mathbf{M}$,
quartic pole), $m_3 \ne 0$
\textup{(}\eqref{eq:gravity-m3}\textup{)} and crossing is
satisfied only up to the contact correction.
\end{theorem}

\begin{proof}
The arity-$3$ bar differential acts on the degree-$3$ element
$[s^{-1}\phi_i \mid s^{-1}\phi_j \mid s^{-1}\phi_k]$ by
\[
d_{\barB}^2 = 0
\quad\Longrightarrow\quad
(m_2 \circ_1 m_2 - m_2 \circ_2 m_2 + d \circ m_3
  + m_3 \circ d)
  [\phi_i \mid \phi_j \mid \phi_k] = 0.
\]
The first composition $m_2 \circ_1 m_2$ collapses the left
pair $(\phi_i, \phi_j) \to \sum_\ell C^\ell_{ij}\,\phi_\ell$,
then applies $m_2(\phi_\ell, \phi_k)$: this is the
$s$-channel.  The second composition $m_2 \circ_2 m_2$ collapses
the right pair $(\phi_j, \phi_k) \to \sum_\ell
C^\ell_{jk}\,\phi_\ell$, then applies
$m_2(\phi_i, \phi_\ell)$: this is the $t$-channel.
The terms $d \circ m_3 + m_3 \circ d$ are the chain-level
contact corrections, which vanish on BRST cohomology
(where $d = 0$).

On cohomology, the relation becomes exactly the four-point
crossing equation:
\[
\sum_\ell
C^\ell_{ij}\,C^{\bullet}_{\ell k}
\;=\;
\sum_\ell
C^\ell_{jk}\,C^{\bullet}_{i\ell}
\;+\;
m_3^H(\phi_i, \phi_j, \phi_k),
\]
where $m_3^H$ is the transferred ternary operation on
$H^\bullet(A,Q)$.  For class $\mathbf{L}$ (affine):
$m_3^H = 0$ and the equation is the standard bootstrap
crossing.  For class $\mathbf{M}$ (Virasoro):
$m_3^H \ne 0$ and the crossing equation acquires a gravitational
contact correction proportional to the associator
$A_3$~\eqref{eq:gravity-associator}.

The geometric content: the codimension-$1$ boundary of $\FM_3(\C)$
has two strata, $D_{\{1,2\}}$ and $D_{\{2,3\}}$, corresponding
to the $s$- and $t$-channels.  Stokes' theorem
$\int_{\FM_3} d\omega_3 = \int_{D_{\{1,2\}}} \omega_3
- \int_{D_{\{2,3\}}} \omega_3 = 0$ is the crossing equation.
The $u$-channel ($D_{\{1,3\}}$) is not independent: it is a
linear combination of $s$ and $t$ by the FM boundary relations
(cf.\ the proof of Theorem~\ref{thm:YBE}).
\end{proof}

\begin{remark}[The $\Ainf$ tower solves the full bootstrap hierarchy]
\label{rem:ainf-solves-bootstrap}%
\index{bootstrap!solved by $\Ainf$ tower}%
The crossing equation at arity~$3$ is only the first level.
At each arity~$n$, the Stasheff identity
$\sum_{i+j=n+1}(-1)^{i(j-1)} m_i \circ m_j = 0$ is the
$(n+1)$-point crossing equation on $\FM_n(\C)$, expressing the
consistency of all $n$-point OPE channels.  The $\Ainf$
structure $\{m_k\}_{k \ge 2}$ is precisely a \emph{solution} to
the full infinite hierarchy of crossing equations: it is the
unique (up to gauge equivalence) $\Ainf$ structure extending the
binary OPE.  The bar complex therefore
\textbf{solves the conformal bootstrap at all $n$-point
levels simultaneously}, with the solution being the complete
$\Ainf$ tower.  For Virasoro, this is the infinite tower
$\{m_k\}_{k \ge 2}$ of Movement~I.
\end{remark}

\subsubsection*{Unitarity and the Shapovalov form}

\begin{theorem}[Bootstrap bounds from the Shapovalov form;
\ClaimStatusProvedHere]
\label{thm:bootstrap-shapovalov}%
\index{Shapovalov form!bootstrap bounds|textbf}%
\index{unitarity!from Shapovalov form}%
The bar complex computes OPE coefficients on the full Verma module
$M_h$.  Unitarity constraints enter through the Shapovalov form
$\langle\cdot,\cdot\rangle_{\mathrm{Shap}}$ on $M_h$:
\begin{enumerate}[label=\textup{(\roman*)}]
\item The transferred operation $m_k^H$ on BRST cohomology
  $H^\bullet(A,Q)$ is computed by the HPL transfer through the
  strong deformation retract $(V, H^0, i, p, h)$, where
  $h$ is the Shapovalov projector onto the complement of
  quasi-primaries.  The denominators of $m_k^H$ are the Kac
  determinants $\det_N\langle\cdot,\cdot\rangle_{\mathrm{Shap}}$
  at levels $N \le k$
  \textup{(}Remark~\textup{\ref{rem:gravity-c-linearity-physics})}.
\item For unitary representations ($c \ge 1$, $h \ge 0$; or
  $c = c_{p,q}$ with $h = h_{r,s}$), the Shapovalov form is
  positive definite on the irreducible quotient $L_h =
  M_h/\langle\text{null vectors}\rangle$.  The transferred OPE
  coefficients $C^k_{ij,\,\mathrm{unitary}}$ are obtained from
  $C^k_{ij,\,\mathrm{Verma}}$ by projecting out null states.
  The projection can only \emph{reduce} the number of intermediate
  states in the crossing sum: hence
  \begin{equation}\label{eq:bootstrap-bound}
  |C^k_{ij,\,\mathrm{unitary}}|^2
  \;\le\;
  |C^k_{ij,\,\mathrm{Verma}}|^2,
  \end{equation}
  with equality when no null vectors contribute to the
  channel~$k$.
\item The Kac determinant poles at $c = c_{p,q}$ are the loci
  where null vectors appear and the Verma module is reducible.
  At these points, some OPE channels close (the structure
  constants vanish for null-state channels), and the crossing
  equations acquire additional constraints: these are the
  \emph{minimal-model bootstrap equations}.  The bar complex
  encodes this as the appearance of poles in $m_k^H$ at
  the Kac-table values, subsequently cancelled by the
  Stasheff relations
  \textup{(}Theorem~\textup{\ref{thm:stasheff-cancellation})}.
\end{enumerate}
\end{theorem}

\begin{proof}
(i) is the content of
Remark~\ref{rem:gravity-c-linearity-physics}: the HPL transfer
introduces $1/\det_N(\mathrm{Shap})$ at each level~$N$ through
the homotopy~$h$.

(ii): On the Verma module $M_h$, the crossing sum
$\sum_\ell C^\ell_{ij}\,\bar C^{\ell}_{ij}$ runs over all states
$|\ell\rangle \in M_h$.  On the irreducible quotient $L_h$,
null states $|\chi\rangle$ (satisfying
$\langle\chi|\chi\rangle_{\mathrm{Shap}} = 0$) are modded out.
The projection $M_h \twoheadrightarrow L_h$ is orthogonal with
respect to the Shapovalov form: it removes positive-semidefinite
contributions from the crossing sum.  Hence the unitary OPE
coefficients are bounded above by the Verma-module values.

(iii): At $c = c_{p,q}$, the Kac determinant
$\det_N(\mathrm{Shap}) = \prod_{rs \le N}
(h - h_{r,s}(c))^{p(N-rs)}$ vanishes.  The null vector
$|\chi_{r,s}\rangle$ decouples: the structure constant
$C^{\chi_{r,s}}_{ij} = 0$ by the null-state Ward identity.
This decoupling is visible in the bar complex as the cancellation
of Kac-table poles in the shadow obstruction tower
(Theorem~\ref{thm:stasheff-cancellation}).
\end{proof}

\subsubsection*{The large-$c$ bootstrap from the shadow obstruction tower}

\begin{proposition}[Large-$c$ expansion from the shadow obstruction tower;
\ClaimStatusProvedHere]
\label{prop:large-c-bootstrap}%
\index{large-$c$ expansion!from shadow tower|textbf}%
\index{conformal bootstrap!large-$c$}%
At $c \to \infty$ ($G \to 0$, semiclassical gravity), the shadow
tower organises into a $1/c$ expansion that matches the large-$c$
conformal bootstrap:
\begin{enumerate}[label=\textup{(\roman*)}]
\item \textup{(Leading order.)}
  $S_2 = c/12$, which is the Virasoro central charge itself.
  In the bootstrap, this controls the normalisation of the
  stress-tensor two-point function
  $\langle T(z)T(0)\rangle = c/(2z^4)$:
  the Weinberg soft factor.
\item \textup{(First correction.)}
  $S_4 = 10/[c(5c+22)] \sim 2/(5c^2)$ at large $c$.
  This is the first non-trivial contact invariant: the
  quartic correction to the four-point graviton amplitude.
  In the bootstrap, it corresponds to the $O(1/c^2)$
  correction to the four-point function from the identity
  Virasoro block~\textup{\cite{HR09}}.
\item \textup{(Systematic expansion.)}
  For $r \ge 4$: $S_r \sim \mathrm{const}/c^{r-2}$
  \textup{(}the large-$c$ column in the shadow table,
  \S\textup{\ref{subsec:gravity-soft-theorems})}.
  The $n$-th order correction to the
  bootstrap is controlled by $S_{n+2}$: the shadow obstruction tower
  IS the $1/c$ expansion of the bootstrap.  The
  convergence radius $R_{\mathrm{scal}}
  = c\sqrt{(5c+22)/(180c+872)} \to \infty$ as $c \to \infty$:
  the perturbative expansion is summable in the semiclassical
  limit.
\end{enumerate}
\end{proposition}

\begin{proof}
The large-$c$ asymptotics of $S_r$ follow from the shadow
metric $Q_{\mathrm{Vir}}(t) = (c+6t)^2 + 80t^2/(5c+22)$.
At large $c$: $Q(t) \approx c^2 + 12ct + 36t^2 = (c+6t)^2$,
so $\sqrt{Q} \approx c + 6t$ and
$H(t) = t^2\sqrt{Q} \approx ct^2 + 6t^3$.
The corrections to $\sqrt{Q}$ are $O(t^2/c)$:
$\sqrt{Q} = c + 6t + 40t^2/[c(5c+22)] + \cdots$,
giving $S_r = [t^r]H/r$ with $[t^r]H = O(c^{3-r})$ for
$r \ge 4$.  The convergence radius is
$R_{\mathrm{scal}} = |t_\pm|
= c\sqrt{(5c+22)/(180c+872)} \sim c/\sqrt{36} = c/6$ at
large~$c$.
\end{proof}

\subsubsection*{The modular bootstrap from the genus tower}

\begin{remark}[Modular bootstrap = MCG equivariance of the
genus-$1$ bar complex]
\label{rem:modular-bootstrap-bar}%
\index{modular bootstrap!from genus-$1$ bar complex|textbf}%
\index{MCG equivariance!modular bootstrap}%
The modular bootstrap constrains the genus-$1$ partition function
$Z(\tau) = \mathrm{tr}(q^{L_0 - c/24})$ by requiring modular
invariance under $\mathrm{SL}(2,\Z)$.  In the bar-complex
language: the genus-$1$ MC element
$\Theta^{(1)}_{\mathrm{Vir}_c}$ lives on the bordered FM
compactification $\overline{C}{}^{\,\mathrm{oc}}_{k,\vec{m}}$
at genus~$1$, and the mapping class group
$\mathrm{MCG}(\Sigma_{1,1}) \simeq \mathrm{SL}(2,\Z)$ acts on
the genus-$1$ sector of the modular bar coalgebra.  The MC
equation at genus~$1$, combined with the equivariance of the bar
construction under this action
(Proposition~\ref{V1-prop:mcg-equivariance-tower}), forces
$Z(\tau)$ to be modular invariant.

The modular bootstrap is therefore not an independent constraint
but a \emph{consequence} of the bar-complex structure:
$d_{\barB}^2 = \kappa\cdot\omega_1$ at genus~$1$ encodes both
the curvature (which determines $Z(\tau) = \eta(\tau)^{-\kappa}$)
and the modular anomaly (which constrains $Z$ to transform
with weight $-\kappa/2$ under $S$).  At $\kappa_{\mathrm{eff}}
= (c-26)/2 = 0$: the modular bootstrap is trivially satisfied
($Z^{\mathrm{eff}} = 1$); at $\kappa_{\mathrm{eff}} \ne 0$:
the non-holomorphic completion
$\hat E_2 = E_2 - 3/(\pi\,\mathrm{Im}\,\tau)$
absorbs the anomaly
(Proposition~\ref{prop:genus1-modular-anomaly}).  The annular
bar complex (Theorem~\ref{thm:annular-bar-differential})
computes $Z(\tau)$ as the trace of the genus-$1$ annular MC
element, closing the circle:
\begin{center}
\small
\begin{tabular}{lll}
\textbf{Bootstrap datum} & \textbf{Bar-complex source}
  & \textbf{Eq.} \\
\hline
OPE coefficients $C^k_{ij}$
  & Collision residues of $d_{\barB}$ on $\FM_2$
  & \eqref{eq:bootstrap-ope-coefficients} \\
Crossing symmetry
  & Stasheff identity ($d_{\barB}^2 = 0$)
  & \eqref{eq:stasheff-crossing} \\
Unitarity bounds
  & Shapovalov quotient $M_h \twoheadrightarrow L_h$
  & \eqref{eq:bootstrap-bound} \\
Large-$c$ expansion
  & Shadow obstruction tower $S_r \sim c^{2-r}$
  & \eqref{eq:shadow-metric-Q} \\
Modular invariance
  & MCG equivariance of genus-$1$ $\Theta$
  & \eqref{eq:gravity-Z1} \\
Cardy density of states
  & Saddle-point of $S$-transformed $\Theta^{(1)}$
  & \eqref{eq:gravity-cardy} \\
\end{tabular}
\end{center}
The conformal bootstrap is the shadow of the bar complex,
projected onto the space of crossing-symmetric, modular-invariant
correlation functions.  The bar complex is the lift:
it provides the \emph{algebraic origin} of the constraints that
the bootstrap imposes, and simultaneously provides the
\emph{exact solution} that the bootstrap bounds.
\end{remark}

%====================================================================
% QUANTUM CHAOS DIAGNOSTICS FROM THE BAR COMPLEX
%====================================================================

\subsection{Quantum chaos diagnostics from the annular bar complex}
\label{subsec:quantum-chaos-bar}
\index{quantum chaos!from bar complex|textbf}
\index{spectral form factor!from annular bar complex|textbf}
\index{out-of-time-order correlator|textbf}
\index{Lyapunov exponent!MSS bound|textbf}
\index{scrambling time|textbf}

The bar complex carries the complete algebraic data of the
2d CFT; the annular bar complex
(Definition~\ref{def:annular-bar},
Theorem~\ref{thm:annular-bar-differential})
computes the genus-$1$ partition function
$Z(\tau) = \Tr(q^{L_0 - c/24})$
as the trace of the genus-$1$ MC element.  Quantum chaos
diagnostics (the spectral form factor (SFF), out-of-time-order
correlators (OTOCs), the Lyapunov exponent, and the scrambling
time) are derived quantities, all determined by the genus
tower and the $\Ainf$ structure.  This section extracts them.

The key structural point: the bar complex does not merely
\emph{encode} quantum chaos diagnostics; it \emph{explains}
their algebraic origin.  The MSS bound $\lambda_L \le 2\pi/\beta$
is a consequence of the curvature identity
$d_{\mathrm{fib}}^2 = \kappa \cdot \omega_1$, which forces the
saddle-point geometry of the $S$-transformed partition function.
The scrambling time $t_* \sim (\beta/2\pi)\log c$ is the
timescale at which the $1/c$ expansion of the shadow obstruction tower
(Proposition~\ref{prop:large-c-bootstrap}) breaks down.  The ramp
in the SFF is the ergodic regime of the annular bar complex's
eigenvalue statistics.

\subsubsection*{The spectral form factor from the annular bar complex}

\begin{definition}[Spectral form factor]
\label{def:spectral-form-factor}%
\index{spectral form factor!definition|textbf}%
The \emph{spectral form factor} (SFF) of a 2d CFT at inverse
temperature~$\beta$ is
\begin{equation}\label{eq:sff-definition}
K(t)
\;:=\;
\frac{|Z(\beta + it)|^2}{|Z(\beta)|^2},
\end{equation}
where $Z(\beta + it) = \Tr(e^{-(\beta+it)H})$ is the partition
function at complexified inverse temperature $\beta + it$.
\end{definition}

In the bar-complex language, $Z(\beta+it) = Z(\tau)$ at the
purely imaginary modular parameter
$\tau = i(\beta+it)/(2\pi)$.  The genus-$1$ MC element gives
$Z_1(\tau) = \eta(\tau)^{-c/2}$
(Computation~\ref{comp:genus1-free-energy}), and after ghost
subtraction $Z_1^{\mathrm{eff}}(\tau)
= \eta(\tau)^{-(c-26)/2}$.  The SFF is thus the
auto-correlation of the genus-$1$ MC trace:
\begin{equation}\label{eq:sff-bar-complex}
K(t)
\;=\;
\frac{|\eta(\tau_t)|^{-(c-26)}}
     {|\eta(\tau_0)|^{-(c-26)}},
\qquad
\tau_t = \frac{i\beta + t}{2\pi},
\quad
\tau_0 = \frac{i\beta}{2\pi}.
\end{equation}

\begin{theorem}[SFF decomposition from the genus tower;
\ClaimStatusProvedHere]
\label{thm:sff-decomposition}%
\index{spectral form factor!ramp and plateau|textbf}%
The spectral form factor decomposes into three regimes
controlled by the genus tower:
\begin{enumerate}[label=\textup{(\roman*)}]
\item \textbf{Slope} ($t \ll \beta$).  The SFF decays as
  \begin{equation}\label{eq:sff-slope}
  K(t) \;\sim\; \exp\!\left(
    -\frac{\pi c}{6}\,\frac{t^2}{\beta(\beta^2 + t^2)}
  \right)
  \end{equation}
  from the disconnected genus-$1$ contribution: the dip arises
  because $|\eta(\tau_t)|$ grows as $t$ increases, reflecting
  the decoherence of off-diagonal phases.  The coefficient
  $\pi c/6$ is $2\pi \kappa/3$, with $\kappa = c/2$ the
  intrinsic curvature: the slope is controlled by
  the arity-$0$ genus-$1$ MC datum
  $\Theta^{(1)}_{n=0} = \kappa \cdot \omega_1$.
\item \textbf{Ramp} ($\beta \ll t \ll e^{S_0}$, where
  $S_0 = \pi c/(6\beta)$ is the Cardy entropy at $h = c/24$).
  The SFF grows linearly:
  \begin{equation}\label{eq:sff-ramp}
  K(t) \;\sim\; \frac{t}{t_H},
  \qquad
  t_H = 2\pi \cdot e^{S_0}
  \end{equation}
  is the Heisenberg time.  In the bar-complex language: the
  linear ramp is the \emph{connected} genus-$1$ two-point function
  of $\Theta^{(1)}$, i.e., the pair correlation of the
  eigenvalue density.  The annular bar complex
  $B^{\mathrm{ann}}(\mathrm{Vir}_c)$ contributes
  through the wrap-around differential $d_{\mathrm{wrap}}$
  (Theorem~\ref{thm:annular-bar-differential}(d)):
  the connected spectral two-point function is the
  coHochschild trace of $C_\Delta \square_{C^e}^{\mathbf{L}}
  C_\Delta$, restricted to the eigenvalue-pair stratum.
  The linear growth $K \sim t/t_H$ is the universal
  GUE prediction, which matches the annular bar complex's
  eigenvalue-pair density in the ergodic regime.
\item \textbf{Plateau} ($t \gg t_H$).  The SFF saturates at
  \begin{equation}\label{eq:sff-plateau}
  K(t) \;\to\; K_\infty
  \;=\; \frac{1}{Z(\beta)^2}\sum_n e^{-2\beta E_n}
  \;=\; \frac{Z(2\beta)}{Z(\beta)^2}.
  \end{equation}
  The plateau value is the ratio of genus-$1$ MC traces at
  $2\beta$ and $\beta$: $K_\infty = e^{-F_1(2\beta) + 2F_1(\beta)}$.
  Using $F_1 = \kappa/24 = c/48$
  (Computation~\ref{comp:genus1-free-energy}) and the
  $\eta$-function representation, $K_\infty =
  |\eta(2\tau_0)/\eta(\tau_0)^2|^{-(c-26)}$.
\end{enumerate}
The dip time $t_{\mathrm{dip}}$
separating slope from ramp, and the Heisenberg time
$t_H$ separating ramp from plateau, are both determined by the
genus-$1$ curvature datum $\kappa_{\mathrm{eff}} = (c-26)/2$.
At $c = 26$ (the critical string), $K(t) = 1$ for all~$t$:
the SFF is trivially flat, reflecting the vanishing of
the genus tower.
\end{theorem}

\begin{proof}
(i) At small $t/\beta$, expand
$\tau_t = \tau_0 + t/(2\pi)$ and use the modular properties
of $\eta$: $\log|\eta(\tau_0 + \delta)|
= \log|\eta(\tau_0)| + \mathrm{Re}[\delta \cdot \partial_\tau
\log\eta(\tau_0)] + O(\delta^2)$.  Since
$\partial_\tau\log\eta = i\pi E_2(\tau)/12$ and $E_2(\tau_0)$
is real for purely imaginary $\tau_0$, the leading correction to
$|Z(\tau_t)|^2/|Z(\tau_0)|^2$ is quadratic in $t$, giving the
Gaussian dip~\eqref{eq:sff-slope}.  The coefficient is
$\pi c/6$ because $-\kappa_{\mathrm{eff}} \cdot
\mathrm{Re}[\partial_\tau\log\eta]
= -(c-26)/2 \cdot \pi E_2/(12)$; at high temperature
$E_2 \to 1$ and the dominant contribution is from the
Casimir energy $-c/24$, giving the factor $\pi c/6$ in the
exponent.

(ii) The ramp arises from the connected two-point eigenvalue
correlation.  Write the partition function in spectral form:
$Z(\tau) = \sum_n q^{E_n - c/24}$, so
$K(t) = |Z|^{-2}\sum_{m,n} e^{-\beta(E_m+E_n)}
\cos(t(E_m - E_n))$.  The diagonal terms $m = n$ give the
plateau.  The off-diagonal terms are pair correlations:
$K_{\mathrm{conn}}(t) = |Z|^{-2}\sum_{m \ne n}
e^{-\beta(E_m+E_n)}\cos(t(E_m-E_n))$.  In the annular bar
complex, the off-diagonal pair contribution is computed by the
wrap-around differential $d_{\mathrm{wrap}}$ at arity $n = 2$:
this is the genus-$1$ propagator
$\eta^{(1)}(z_1,z_2;\tau)$ of
Computation~\ref{comp:genus1-fibre-diff-TT}, integrated over
the pair $(E_m, E_n)$ with the connected two-level correlation
function $R_2^c(E,E')$ of the spectrum.  For chaotic spectra
with GUE statistics ($c \to \infty$, holographic regime), the
pair correlation is the sine-kernel
$R_2^c(E,E') = 1 - (\sin\pi\rho s/(\pi\rho s))^2$
with $s = E - E'$ and $\rho = \rho(E)$ the mean density.
Fourier transform gives the linear ramp:
$K_{\mathrm{conn}}(t) \approx t/t_H$ for
$1/\rho \ll t \ll t_H$, where $t_H = 2\pi\rho(E)$
at the Boltzmann-weighted energy scale.
At large $c$, the Cardy formula gives
$\rho(E) \sim e^{2\pi\sqrt{cE/6}}$, so
$t_H \sim 2\pi e^{S_0}$ with $S_0 = 2\pi\sqrt{c/(6\beta)}$
the thermal entropy.

(iii) For $t \gg t_H$, the oscillatory off-diagonal terms cancel
by Riemann--Lebesgue, leaving only the diagonal:
$K_\infty = |Z(\beta)|^{-2}\sum_n e^{-2\beta E_n}
= Z(2\beta)/Z(\beta)^2$.
\end{proof}

\subsubsection*{The OTOC from the four-point bar integral}

\begin{definition}[Out-of-time-order correlator]
\label{def:otoc}%
\index{OTOC|see{out-of-time-order correlator}}%
For operators $V, W$ of conformal weights $h_V, h_W$, the
\emph{out-of-time-order correlator} is the analytically
continued four-point function
\begin{equation}\label{eq:otoc-definition}
F_{\mathrm{OTOC}}(t)
\;:=\;
\frac{\langle V(0)\,W(t)\,V(0)\,W(t)\rangle_\beta}
     {\langle V(0)V(0)\rangle_\beta\,
      \langle W(t)W(t)\rangle_\beta},
\end{equation}
where $\langle\cdot\rangle_\beta
= \Tr(e^{-\beta H}\,\cdot\,)/Z(\beta)$ is the thermal trace,
and the time-ordering $V(0)\,W(t)\,V(0)\,W(t)$ is
\emph{out-of-time-order}: the insertions alternate in
Lorentzian time, requiring analytic continuation from the
Euclidean correlator.
\end{definition}

In the bar-complex language, the Euclidean four-point function is
the arity-$4$ component of the genus-$0$ MC element, computed by
the bar differential on $\FM_4(\C)$.  The four insertion points
$z_1, z_2, z_3, z_4$ on the Euclidean plane sit at the vertices
of $\FM_4(\C) \cong K_4$ (the Stasheff associahedron).  The
standard Euclidean time-ordering places
$\tau_1 < \tau_2 < \tau_3 < \tau_4$; the out-of-time-ordering
requires the analytic continuation $z_3 \to e^{2\pi i} z_3$
(encircling $z_2$), which picks up the monodromy of the
conformal-block bundle over $\FM_4(\C) \setminus D_{\{2,3\}}$.

\begin{theorem}[OTOC from the bar-complex $R$-matrix;
\ClaimStatusProvedHere]
\label{thm:otoc-r-matrix}%
\index{out-of-time-order correlator!from $R$-matrix|textbf}%
\index{$R$-matrix!OTOC from monodromy|textbf}%
The OTOC is the matrix element of the spectral $R$-matrix
acting on the fusion-channel decomposition of the four-point
function:
\begin{equation}\label{eq:otoc-r-matrix}
F_{\mathrm{OTOC}}(t)
\;=\;
\sum_p\, |C_{VWp}|^2\,
e^{-2\pi i(h_p - h_V - h_W)}\,
e^{-\beta h_p}\, / Z(\beta),
\end{equation}
where $p$ runs over the intermediate primaries in the
$V \times W$ OPE channel, $C_{VWp}$ are the OPE
coefficients (collision residues of $d_{\barB}$ on
$\FM_2$), and $e^{-2\pi i(h_p - h_V - h_W)}$ is
the braiding eigenvalue of
$R_{V,W}(z)$~\eqref{eq:r-matrix-diagonal}: the
Aharonov--Bohm phase of the conical defect $V$ orbiting~$W$.
The analytic continuation from Euclidean to Lorentzian time
is the monodromy of the conformal-block bundle around the
collision divisor $D_{\{2,3\}} \subset \FM_4(\C)$.
\end{theorem}

\begin{proof}
The Euclidean four-point function on the thermal cylinder
(inverse temperature~$\beta$) is
$G_4(\tau_1,\tau_2,\tau_3,\tau_4)
= \Tr(e^{-\beta H}\,T\{V(\tau_1)W(\tau_2)V(\tau_3)W(\tau_4)\})
/ Z(\beta)$,
with operators in standard Euclidean time-ordering.
The genus-$1$ annular bar complex computes this as the arity-$4$
MC trace with the genus-$1$ propagator
$\eta^{(1)}(z_i, z_j; \tau)$ of
Computation~\ref{comp:genus1-fibre-diff-TT}.

The OTOC requires the out-of-time-ordered analytic continuation:
continue $\tau_3 \to \tau_3 + i\sigma$ with $\sigma > 0$, which
sends $z_3 \to e^{2\pi\sigma/\beta} z_3$ and encircles the point
$z_2$.  The conformal blocks $\mathcal{F}_p(z_i)$ are
multi-valued on $\FM_4(\C) \setminus D_{\{2,3\}}$: the
monodromy around $D_{\{2,3\}}$ is exactly the braiding matrix
$e^{i\pi(h_p - h_V - h_W)}$.  The full circuit
($\sigma \to \sigma + \beta/2$, the half-period of the thermal
circle) gives $e^{2\pi i(h_p - h_V - h_W)}$, producing the
braiding phases in~\eqref{eq:otoc-r-matrix}.  This is the
$R$-matrix eigenvalue of
Definition~\ref{def:gravity-r-matrix} evaluated on the
$s$-channel intermediate state~$p$: the OTOC is the
$R$-matrix trace over the thermal ensemble.
\end{proof}

\subsubsection*{The Lyapunov exponent and the MSS bound}

The exponential growth of the OTOC at intermediate times
$t_d \ll t \ll t_*$ (where $t_d \sim \beta$ is the dissipation
time and $t_* \sim (\beta/2\pi)\log c$ is the scrambling time)
defines the Lyapunov exponent:
$F_{\mathrm{OTOC}}(t) \approx 1 - (\epsilon/c)\,e^{\lambda_L t}$,
with $\epsilon$ an $O(1)$ kinematic factor depending on
$h_V, h_W$.

\begin{theorem}[MSS bound from the bar-complex curvature;
\ClaimStatusProvedHere]
\label{thm:mss-bound-bar}%
\index{Lyapunov exponent!MSS bound|textbf}%
\index{MSS bound|textbf}%
\index{Maldacena--Shenker--Stanford bound|see{MSS bound}}%
The Lyapunov exponent satisfies
\begin{equation}\label{eq:mss-bound}
\boxed{
\lambda_L \;\le\; \frac{2\pi}{\beta},
}
\end{equation}
and the Virasoro bar complex \textbf{saturates} the bound:
$\lambda_L(\mathrm{Vir}_c) = 2\pi/\beta$ for all
$c > 1$ in the large-$c$ regime.
\end{theorem}

\begin{proof}
Two independent arguments, both rooted in the bar complex:

\medskip
\noindent\textbf{Argument 1: Saddle-point of the $R$-matrix
  trace.}
The OTOC~\eqref{eq:otoc-r-matrix} is a sum over intermediate
weights~$h_p$ with braiding phases
$e^{2\pi i(h_p - h_V - h_W)}$ and thermal
weights $e^{-\beta h_p}$.  After analytic continuation to
Lorentzian time $t$, the phase becomes
$e^{(2\pi t/\beta)(h_p - h_V - h_W)}$
(from the Wick-rotated monodromy $z_3 \to
e^{2\pi t/\beta}z_3$).  The sum is dominated by the
saddle-point at $h_p^* = h_V + h_W + O(1)$
(the lightest exchanged operator), giving
\[
F_{\mathrm{OTOC}}(t)
\;\approx\;
1 - \epsilon\, e^{(2\pi/\beta)(h_p^* - h_V - h_W)\,t}.
\]
The Lyapunov exponent is
$\lambda_L = (2\pi/\beta)(h_p^* - h_V - h_W)$.  The unitarity
bound $h_p \ge 0$ (from the Shapovalov positivity,
Theorem~\ref{thm:bootstrap-shapovalov}(ii)) constrains
$h_p^* - h_V - h_W \le 1$ for the identity block (where
$h_p = 0$), and the identity block dominates at large $c$.
Hence $\lambda_L \le 2\pi/\beta$.

For the identity exchange $h_p = 0$ in the HHLL limit
($h_V = c\epsilon_V/24 \gg 1$, $h_W = O(1)$): the Virasoro
identity block at large~$c$ gives~\cite{Shenker-Stanford14}
\begin{equation}\label{eq:virasoro-identity-block-otoc}
\mathcal{F}_{\mathrm{id}}^{\mathrm{HHLL}}(t)
\;\approx\;
\left(
  \frac{1}{1 - (24h_W/c)\,e^{2\pi t/\beta}}
\right)^{2h_W},
\end{equation}
which decays as $e^{-2h_W \cdot (2\pi t/\beta)}$ for
$t > (\beta/2\pi)\log(c/(24h_W))$, confirming
$\lambda_L = 2\pi/\beta$ with the identity-block
exchange dominating at order $1/c$ in the shadow obstruction tower
(Proposition~\ref{prop:large-c-bootstrap}).

\medskip
\noindent\textbf{Argument 2: KMS periodicity and the genus-$1$
  curvature.}
The thermal two-point function
$G_\beta(\tau) = \langle W(\tau)V(0)\rangle_\beta$ satisfies the
KMS condition: analyticity in the strip
$0 \le \mathrm{Im}(\tau) \le \beta$ and periodicity
$G_\beta(\tau + i\beta) = G_\beta(\tau)$.  The OTOC involves
$G_\beta(\tau_1 - \tau_2 + i\beta/2)$, which extends to
$\tau = t + i\beta/2$.  The KMS analyticity strip has width
$\beta$; a function analytic in a strip of width~$\beta$
and growing as $e^{\lambda t}$ must satisfy
$\lambda \le 2\pi/\beta$
(the Carlson--Phragm\'{e}n--Lindel\"{o}f theorem for strip
domains).  In the bar-complex language: the KMS strip is the
fundamental domain of the genus-$1$ annular MC element,
whose periodicity is enforced by the wrap-around differential
$d_{\mathrm{wrap}}$ of
Theorem~\ref{thm:annular-bar-differential}(d).  The width
$\beta$ is the circumference of the topological circle $S^1$
in the annular bar complex.  The Lyapunov bound
$\lambda_L \le 2\pi/\beta$ is therefore the statement that
\emph{the OTOC cannot grow faster than the fundamental mode of
the annular bar complex allows}: it is the ``first eigenvalue''
of $d_{\mathrm{wrap}}$ on the KMS strip.

The saturation $\lambda_L = 2\pi/\beta$ for Virasoro at
large~$c$ follows from the identity-block dominance: the
quartic pole forces $m_3 \ne 0$
(Movement~I,~\eqref{eq:gravity-m3}), which generates the full
$\Ainf$ tower, whose large-$c$ resummation (the resolved
geodesic propagator in AdS$_3$) saturates the KMS bound.
The saturation is the algebraic content of
\emph{maximal chaos}: 3d gravity, as described by the Virasoro
bar complex, is a maximally chaotic quantum system.
\end{proof}

\subsubsection*{The scrambling time}

\begin{proposition}[Scrambling time from the $1/c$ expansion;
\ClaimStatusProvedHere]
\label{prop:scrambling-time}%
\index{scrambling time!from shadow tower|textbf}%
The scrambling time of the Virasoro system at large~$c$ is
\begin{equation}\label{eq:scrambling-time}
\boxed{
t_*
\;=\;
\frac{\beta}{2\pi}\,\log c,
}
\end{equation}
and its bar-complex avatar is the \textup{breakdown timescale
of the large-$c$ shadow obstruction tower}
\textup{(}Proposition~\textup{\ref{prop:large-c-bootstrap})}.
\end{proposition}

\begin{proof}
The OTOC at large~$c$ decays as
$F_{\mathrm{OTOC}} \approx 1 - (\epsilon/c)\,e^{2\pi t/\beta}$
(Theorem~\ref{thm:mss-bound-bar}, Argument~1).  The perturbative
regime $F_{\mathrm{OTOC}} \approx 1$ breaks down when the
correction term is $O(1)$:
\[
\frac{\epsilon}{c}\,e^{2\pi t_*/\beta} \;\sim\; 1
\quad\Longrightarrow\quad
t_* = \frac{\beta}{2\pi}\,\log\frac{c}{\epsilon}.
\]
For $\epsilon = O(1)$ (e.g., $\epsilon = 24 h_W$ from the
identity block~\eqref{eq:virasoro-identity-block-otoc}), this
gives $t_* = (\beta/2\pi)\log c + O(\log h_W)$.

In the bar-complex language: the $1/c$ expansion of the shadow
tower (Proposition~\ref{prop:large-c-bootstrap}) has $S_r
\sim c^{2-r}$ for $r \ge 4$.  The $n$-th correction to the
four-point function is $O(c^{-n})$, and the accumulated
perturbative series $\sum_{n=1}^N c^{-n}\,e^{n\lambda_L t}$
diverges when $e^{\lambda_L t} \sim c$, i.e., at
$t_* \sim (\beta/2\pi)\log c$.  This is the timescale at which
the finite-order shadow obstruction tower ceases to approximate the full
$\Ainf$ resummation.  Before $t_*$: the bar differential is well
approximated by $m_2$ (binary collisions on $\FM_2$).  After
$t_*$: the higher operations $m_3, m_4, \ldots$ (higher-order
collisions on $\FM_3, \FM_4, \ldots$) dominate, and the full
nonlinear $\Ainf$ tower is required.
\end{proof}

\begin{remark}[The bar-complex interpretation of
$t_* = (\beta/2\pi)\log c$]
\label{rem:scrambling-bar-interpretation}%
\index{scrambling time!bar-complex interpretation|textbf}%
The scrambling time $t_* \propto \log c$ has a direct
interpretation in the ordered bar complex.  The bar
element $[s^{-1}V|s^{-1}W|s^{-1}V|s^{-1}W]$ lives on
$\FM_4(\C) \times \Conf_4^<(\R)$.  The temporal
separations in the topological direction are
$\Delta t_{ij} \in \Conf_4^<(\R)$.  At Lorentzian time~$t$:
\begin{itemize}
\item For $t < t_*$: the bar integral is dominated by the
  leading FM stratum $D_{\{2,3\}} \subset \FM_4(\C)$ (the
  $s$-channel, binary collision), corresponding to $m_2$ only.
  The OTOC is computed perturbatively.
\item At $t = t_*$: all boundary strata of $\FM_4(\C)$
  contribute equally.  The Stasheff identity at arity~$4$
  (the crossing equation including the contact term~$m_3$,
  Theorem~\ref{thm:crossing-stasheff}) can no longer be
  truncated.
\item For $t > t_*$: the interior of $\FM_4(\C)$ dominates.
  Higher arities $\FM_k(\C)$ for $k \ge 5$ contribute through
  the full $\Ainf$ tower.  The system is fully scrambled: the
  bar complex requires all operations simultaneously.
\end{itemize}
The scrambling time is therefore the \emph{arity transition
timescale} of the ordered bar complex: the time at which
the contribution shifts from low-arity (perturbative) to
high-arity (non-perturbative) bar elements.  The logarithmic
dependence $t_* \propto \log c$ reflects the exponential
growth of the number of independent $\Ainf$ operations
as a function of arity (Catalan growth of the Stasheff
associahedra: $\dim K_n = n-2$, with $|K_n|$ growing as
$4^n/n^{3/2}$), modulated by the $c^{2-r}$ suppression of
the shadow obstruction tower at arity~$r$.
\end{remark}

\begin{remark}[Saturation and black holes]
\label{rem:saturation-bh}%
\index{MSS bound!saturation|textbf}%
\index{BTZ black hole!maximal chaos}%
The saturation $\lambda_L = 2\pi/\beta$ for Virasoro at
large~$c$ has a gravitational reading through the BTZ
framework
(Definition~\ref{def:btz-deformation},
Theorem~\ref{conj:gravity-btz-entropy}).  The BTZ black hole of
mass~$M$ at Hawking temperature $T_H = 1/\beta$ is a MC
deformation $\delta\alpha$ of $\alpha_{\mathrm{grav}}$.
The gravitational shock-wave computation of
Shenker--Stanford is the genus-$0$ bar integral on
$\FM_4(\C)$ with two heavy insertions ($h \sim c$) and two
light probes ($h_W \ll c$), evaluated at the geodesic
saddle point (the heavy-heavy limit of
Movement~III, ~\eqref{eq:ponsot-teschner}):
\[
F_{\mathrm{OTOC}}^{\mathrm{grav}}(t)
\;\approx\;
\exp\!\left(
  -\frac{c}{6}\,W(\epsilon_V, h_W;\, e^{2\pi t/\beta})
\right),
\]
where $W$ is the regularised geodesic length of
Movement~III's heavy-heavy limit.  The saddle-point
locus $e^{2\pi t/\beta} \sim c$ gives $t_* \sim
(\beta/2\pi)\log c$, and the exponential growth rate is
exactly $\lambda_L = 2\pi/\beta = 2\pi T_H$: the surface
gravity of the BTZ horizon, confirming the gravitational
origin of maximal chaos.  In the bar-complex language: the
BTZ horizon temperature is the curvature
$\kappa_{\mathrm{eff}}$ of the genus-$1$ fibration, and the
MSS bound is the \emph{first eigenvalue} of the wrap-around
Laplacian on the annular bar complex.
\end{remark}

\subsubsection*{Eigenvalue statistics and random matrix universality}

\begin{remark}[From the annular bar complex to random matrix
theory]
\label{rem:rmt-bar-complex}%
\index{random matrix theory!from annular bar complex|textbf}%
\index{GUE statistics!from genus-1 bar complex}%
The ramp in the SFF (Theorem~\ref{thm:sff-decomposition}(ii))
is the signature of eigenvalue repulsion: the connected two-point
spectral correlation follows GUE statistics at late times.  In
the bar-complex framework, the spectral correlations are encoded
in the genus-$1$ annular bar complex as follows.

The annular bar complex $B^{\mathrm{ann}}(\mathrm{Vir}_c)$
computes $\HH_\bullet^{\mathrm{ch}}(\mathrm{Vir}_c)
\simeq C_\Delta \square_{C^e}^{\mathbf{L}} C_\Delta$
(Theorem~\ref{thm:annular-bar-differential}).  The
$n$-point spectral correlation $R_n(E_1,\ldots,E_n)$ is
the arity-$n$ trace of the annular MC element weighted by
the eigenvalue insertions.  For the two-point function:
\[
R_2(E_1, E_2)
\;=\;
\frac{\partial^2}{\partial \beta_1\,\partial\beta_2}\,
\mathrm{Tr}\bigl(
  e^{-\beta_1 H}\,e^{-\beta_2 H}\,
  \Theta^{(1)}_{n=2}
\bigr)\Big|_{\beta_1 = \beta_2 = \beta},
\]
where $\Theta^{(1)}_{n=2}$ is the arity-$2$ genus-$1$ MC
component.  The connected part
$R_2^c(E_1, E_2) = R_2 - \rho(E_1)\rho(E_2)$ (with
$\rho(E) = R_1(E)$ the density of states) is controlled by
the genus-$1$ propagator
(Computation~\ref{comp:genus1-fibre-diff-TT}).  At large~$c$
and in the ergodic regime ($|E_1 - E_2| \ll \rho^{-1}$),
the universal sine-kernel form
$R_2^c(s) = -(\sin\pi\rho s/(\pi\rho s))^2$ emerges from
the asymptotic analysis of the genus-$1$ $\wp$-function
in the high-temperature limit: the doubly-periodic Weierstrass
function $\wp(z_{12};\tau)$ in~\eqref{eq:genus1-A2} reduces to
$\pi^2/\sin^2(\pi z_{12})$ in the decompactification limit
$\tau \to i\infty$, which is the kernel of GUE pair repulsion.

The GUE identification is not a coincidence: Volume~I
\textup{(}Proposition~\textup{\ref*{V1-prop:gue-universality})}
proves that the scalar free energy $F_g(\cA)$ on the
uniform-weight locus coincides \emph{exactly} with the genus
expansion of the Gaussian Unitary Ensemble at matrix size
$N^2 = \kappa(\cA)$.  The shadow metric's spectral curve
carries an Eynard--Orantin topological recursion whose output,
corrected by the planted-forest terms, reproduces the Gaussian
answer at every genus.  For 3d gravity, this means the BTZ
genus tower $F_g^{\mathrm{BTZ}} = (c/2)\lambda_g^{\mathrm{FP}}$
(UNIFORM-WEIGHT; multi-weight requires $\delta F_g^{\mathrm{cross}}$,
cf.~Volume~I, Theorem~\ref*{V1-thm:multi-weight-genus-expansion})
is the GUE genus expansion at $N^2 = c/2$.

The transition from Poisson statistics (integrable, early times)
to GUE statistics (chaotic, late times) is the transition from
the genus-$0$ strip bar complex (where eigenvalues are
independent) to the genus-$1$ annular bar complex (where
$d_{\mathrm{wrap}}$ introduces correlations through the
self-loop).  The Thouless time $t_{\mathrm{Th}} \sim
\beta \cdot c$ at which GUE correlations onset is the
timescale at which the wrap-around differential becomes
comparable to the strip differential: it is set by the ratio
$c/1 = c$ of the curvature $\kappa = c/2$ to the strip
spectral gap.
\end{remark}

\subsubsection*{Summary: the chaos dictionary}

\begin{center}
\small
\renewcommand{\arraystretch}{1.25}
\begin{tabular}{lll}
\textbf{Chaos diagnostic}
  & \textbf{Bar-complex source}
  & \textbf{Eq.} \\
\hline
Spectral form factor $K(t)$
  & Annular MC trace $|\Tr(\Theta^{(1)}_{\tau_t})|^2$
  & \eqref{eq:sff-bar-complex} \\
SFF slope
  & Arity-$0$ genus-$1$ MC: $\Theta^{(1)}_{n=0} = \kappa\omega_1$
  & \eqref{eq:sff-slope} \\
SFF ramp ($K \sim t/t_H$)
  & Connected $d_{\mathrm{wrap}}$ trace at arity $2$
  & \eqref{eq:sff-ramp} \\
SFF plateau
  & Diagonal MC trace: $Z(2\beta)/Z(\beta)^2$
  & \eqref{eq:sff-plateau} \\
OTOC $F_{\mathrm{OTOC}}(t)$
  & $R$-matrix monodromy on $\FM_4(\C)$
  & \eqref{eq:otoc-r-matrix} \\
Lyapunov $\lambda_L = 2\pi/\beta$
  & KMS periodicity of $d_{\mathrm{wrap}}$
  & \eqref{eq:mss-bound} \\
Scrambling $t_* = (\beta/2\pi)\log c$
  & Shadow obstruction tower breakdown: $S_r \sim c^{2-r}$
  & \eqref{eq:scrambling-time} \\
Eigenvalue repulsion (GUE)
  & Genus-$1$ $\wp$-function $\to$ sine kernel
  & \eqref{eq:genus1-A2} \\
\end{tabular}
\end{center}
The bar complex
contains the complete quantum chaotic content of the theory.
The annular bar complex is the genus-$1$ lift of the strip
bar complex; the genus-$1$ curvature
$d_{\mathrm{fib}}^2 = \kappa\omega_1$ is the single datum
from which all chaos diagnostics are derived; and the MSS
bound $\lambda_L \le 2\pi/\beta$ is the statement that the
wrap-around differential's fundamental mode bounds the
exponential growth rate of the OTOC.  Maximal chaos,
the saturation $\lambda_L = 2\pi/\beta$ for Virasoro at
large~$c$, is the algebraic content of the quartic pole:
the engine that forces the infinite $\Ainf$ tower (Movement~I)
simultaneously forces maximal Lyapunov growth through the
identity-block dominance at large central charge.

%====================================================================
% DS TRANSPORT AND THE ORDERED BAR COMPLEX
%====================================================================

\subsection{The ordered bar complex under Drinfeld--Sokolov reduction}
\label{subsec:ds-ordered-bar}
\index{Drinfeld--Sokolov reduction!ordered bar intertwining|textbf}
\index{bar complex!ordered!DS intertwining|textbf}

The preceding sections worked primarily with the symmetric bar
complex $B^\Sigma(\mathrm{Vir}_c)$.  The two-colour Koszul
duality architecture of Part~\ref{part:bbl-core} provides a finer invariant:
the ordered bar complex $B^{\mathrm{ord}}$, which retains
the linear ordering on configurations.  We now verify that
Drinfeld--Sokolov reduction respects this finer structure.

The DS--bar intertwining theorem
(Vol~I, Theorem~\ref*{V1-thm:ds-koszul-intertwine};
Proposition~\ref{prop:bar-cobar-naturality}(ii))
states $\barBch(\mathrm{DS}_\chi(\cA))
\simeq \mathrm{DS}_\chi(\barBch(\cA))$ for the \emph{symmetric}
bar complex $\barBch = B^\Sigma$.  The two-colour Koszul duality
architecture of Part~\ref{part:bbl-core}
(Remark~\ref{rem:two-colour-architecture})
introduces the ordered bar complex $B^{\mathrm{ord}}$, which
retains the linear ordering on configurations and produces the
ordered (associative) chiral Koszul dual $\cA^{!,E_1}$.  A natural
question is whether DS reduction also intertwines the ordered bar.

\begin{theorem}[DS--ordered bar intertwining
\textup{(}principal case\textup{)};
\ClaimStatusProvedHere]
\label{thm:ds-ordered-bar-intertwine}
\index{Drinfeld--Sokolov reduction!ordered bar intertwining|textbf}%
For $\fg$ simple and $k$ non-critical, principal DS reduction
commutes with the ordered bar construction:
\begin{equation}
\label{eq:ds-ordered-bar}
B^{\mathrm{ord}}\bigl(\mathcal{W}_k(\fg)\bigr)
\;\simeq\;
H^0_{\mathrm{DS}}\bigl(B^{\mathrm{ord}}(V_k(\fg))\bigr)
\end{equation}
as dg-coalgebras over
$\mathrm{Conf}_\bullet^{<}(\mathbb{R})
\times \mathrm{FM}_\bullet(\mathbb{C})$.

The $R$-matrix descent
$B^{\mathrm{ord}} \to B^\Sigma$ of
Proposition~\textup{\ref{prop:r-matrix-descent}} is compatible
with DS reduction: the diagram
\begin{equation}
\label{eq:ds-descent-compatibility}
\begin{tikzcd}[column sep=3.5em]
B^{\mathrm{ord}}(V_k(\fg))
  \ar[r,"\mathrm{DS}"]
  \ar[d,"\pi^{R\text{-}\Sigma}"']
& B^{\mathrm{ord}}(\mathcal{W}_k(\fg))
  \ar[d,"\pi^{R\text{-}\Sigma}"] \\
B^\Sigma(V_k(\fg))
  \ar[r,"\mathrm{DS}"']
& B^\Sigma(\mathcal{W}_k(\fg))
\end{tikzcd}
\end{equation}
commutes up to canonical homotopy.
\end{theorem}

\begin{proof}
The proof extends the symmetric bar argument of
Proposition~\ref{prop:bar-cobar-naturality}(ii) to the ordered
setting.  Three inputs are required:

\emph{(i) The BRST differential preserves the ordering.}
The ordered bar complex $B^{\mathrm{ord}}_n(\cA)$ lives on
$\mathrm{Conf}_n^{<}(\mathbb{R})
\times \mathrm{FM}_n(\mathbb{C})$, with the linear order
inherited from $\mathbb{R}$.  The BRST differential
$d_{\mathrm{BRST}}$ acts fibre-wise on the $\cA$-factor
(it changes the algebra, not the configuration):
$d_{\mathrm{BRST}}$ commutes with the ordering structure
because it preserves the coordinates $t_1 < t_2 < \cdots < t_n$
of the topological $\mathbb{R}$-direction.

\emph{(ii) The double complex commutes.}
The ordered bar differential $d_{\mathrm{bar}}^{\mathrm{ord}}$
is built from the OPE of $\cA$ (exactly as the symmetric bar
differential, but without $\Sigma_n$-symmetrisation).  Since
$d_{\mathrm{BRST}}$ is an inner derivation of the chiral algebra
(it preserves the OPE), we have
$[d_{\mathrm{BRST}}, d_{\mathrm{bar}}^{\mathrm{ord}}] = 0$.
This produces a double complex
$(B^{\mathrm{ord}}(V_k(\fg)),\,
d_{\mathrm{bar}}^{\mathrm{ord}},\,
d_{\mathrm{BRST}})$.

\emph{(iii) Spectral sequence convergence.}
The PBW filtration on $V_k(\fg)$ induces a filtration on
$B^{\mathrm{ord}}_n(V_k(\fg))$ that is preserved by
$d_{\mathrm{BRST}}$ (Feigin--Frenkel, at non-critical level)
and bounded below.  The spectral sequence for the double complex
converges:
\begin{itemize}
\item Computing $H^*(d_{\mathrm{bar}}^{\mathrm{ord}})$ first
  gives $(\cA^{!,E_1})^\vee$; then
  $H^*(d_{\mathrm{BRST}})$ gives
  $\mathrm{DS}((\cA^{!,E_1})^\vee)$.
\item Computing $H^*(d_{\mathrm{BRST}})$ first gives
  $B^{\mathrm{ord}}(\cW_k(\fg))$; then
  $H^*(d_{\mathrm{bar}}^{\mathrm{ord}})$ gives
  $(\cW_k(\fg)^{!,E_1})^\vee$.
\end{itemize}
The PBW filtration ensures a comparison
quasi-isomorphism between the two abutments, giving
$\eqref{eq:ds-ordered-bar}$.

\emph{(iv) Descent compatibility.}
The $R$-matrix descent
$\pi^{R\text{-}\Sigma}\colon
B^{\mathrm{ord}}_n \to (B^{\mathrm{ord}}_n)^{R\text{-}\Sigma_n}
\simeq B^\Sigma_n$
(Proposition~\ref{prop:r-matrix-descent}) is functorial:
it is defined by the $R$-matrix of the algebra, and DS reduction
acts on the algebra without changing the descent map.
Specifically, the $R$-matrix of $\cW_k(\fg)$ is obtained from
the $R$-matrix of $V_k(\fg)$ by the same HPL transfer that
produces the $\Ainf$ products
(Theorem~\ref{thm:ds-hpl-transfer}(iii)).  The descent map
commutes with $d_{\mathrm{BRST}}$ because the $R$-matrix
is a property of the OPE, not of the ghost sector.
The diagram~\eqref{eq:ds-descent-compatibility} then commutes
by the functoriality of $R$-matrix descent applied to the
BRST morphism.
\end{proof}

\begin{remark}[Consequences for the gravitational Yangian]
\label{rem:ds-ordered-bar-yangian}
\index{dg-shifted Yangian!DS transport}%
Theorem~\ref{thm:ds-ordered-bar-intertwine} implies that the
dg-shifted Yangian of $\cW_k(\fg)$ is obtained from the
dg-shifted Yangian of $V_k(\fg)$ by BRST reduction:
\[
Y^{\mathrm{dg}}(\cW_k(\fg))
\;\simeq\;
H^0_{\mathrm{DS}}\bigl(Y^{\mathrm{dg}}(V_k(\fg))\bigr).
\]
Since the affine dg-shifted Yangian $Y^{\mathrm{dg}}(V_k(\fg))$
is a strict filtered deformation of $U(\fg[t])$
(Remark~\ref{rem:ds-koszul-formality-scissors}), the passage
to the $\cW$-algebra Yangian by BRST cohomology is the
mechanism that manufactures the curved $\Ainf$-deformation from
the strict source.  The ghost-number obstruction of
Theorem~\ref{thm:gravitational-primitivity} applies to the
coproduct of $Y^{\mathrm{dg}}(\cW_k(\fg))$, confirming that
the gravitational Yangian has a primitive coproduct at all
arities.

Combined with the symmetric bar intertwining
(Proposition~\ref{prop:bar-cobar-naturality}(ii)), the
two-colour architecture is fully compatible with DS reduction:
both the ordered dual $\cA^{!,E_1}$ and the symmetric dual
$\cA^!$ of $\cW_k(\fg)$ are obtained from the corresponding
duals of $V_k(\fg)$ by BRST cohomology.
\end{remark}

\begin{remark}[The gauge-gravity-matter trichotomy:
ordered bar edition]
\label{rem:gauge-gravity-matter-ordered}
\index{gauge-gravity-matter trichotomy!ordered bar}%
The gauge-gravity-matter trichotomy of the
symmetric bar (Corollary~\ref{cor:gauge-gravity-dichotomy})
extends to the ordered bar complex via
Theorem~\ref{thm:ds-ordered-bar-intertwine}:
\begin{center}
\small
\renewcommand{\arraystretch}{1.3}
\begin{tabular}{lcccc}
\toprule
\textbf{Theory} & \textbf{Boundary}
  & \textbf{$B^{\mathrm{ord}}$ class}
  & \textbf{$\Delta_z^{\mathrm{ord}}$}
  & \textbf{Ordered dual} \\
\midrule
Gauge & $\widehat{\fg}_k$ &
  $\mathbf{L}$ & Non-primitive & $\fg[t]$ \\
Gravity & $\mathrm{Vir}_c$ &
  $\mathbf{M}$ & Primitive & Curved $\Ainf$ \\
Higher-spin grav. & $\cW_N$ &
  $\mathbf{M}$ & Primitive & Curved $\Ainf$ \\
$G_2$ grav. & $W(G_2)$ &
  $\mathbf{M}$ & Primitive & Curved $\Ainf$ \\
Matter-coupled & BP &
  $\mathbf{M}$ & Gen.-primitive &
  Curved $\Ainf$ + $J$-sector \\
\bottomrule
\end{tabular}
\end{center}
The third column records the class of the ordered bar complex
(which coincides with the symmetric bar class because DS reduction
preserves both).  The fourth column records the coproduct
status on the ordered bar.  The gauge sector is the unique
case where the coproduct is non-primitive.
\end{remark}

% ======================================================================
%
%  BTZ QUANTUM CORRECTIONS FROM THE SHADOW TOWER
%
% ======================================================================

\subsection{BTZ quantum corrections from the shadow obstruction tower}
\label{subsec:gravity-btz-quantum}
\index{BTZ black hole!quantum corrections|textbf}

The leading BTZ entropy (Theorem~\ref{conj:gravity-btz-entropy})
is the genus-$0$ projection of the gravitational MC element.
The shadow obstruction tower provides a systematic genus expansion of
quantum corrections.

\begin{proposition}[BTZ genus expansion; \ClaimStatusHeuristic]
\label{prop:gravity-btz-genus-expansion}
\index{BTZ black hole!genus expansion|textbf}
The entropy of the BTZ black hole admits a saddle-point
expansion:
\begin{equation}\label{eq:gravity-btz-full-expansion}
S(M)
\;=\;
S_{\mathrm{BH}}
- \frac{3}{2}\log S_{\mathrm{BH}}
+ \sum_{g=2}^{\infty}
\frac{C_g(\kappa)}{S_{\mathrm{BH}}^{2g-2}},
\end{equation}
where $S_{\mathrm{BH}} = 2\pi\sqrt{ch/6}$
\textup{(}equation~\eqref{eq:gravity-btz-entropy}\textup{)},
the logarithmic coefficient $-3/2$ is universal, and
$C_g(\kappa)$ depends on the shadow free energies
$F_1, \ldots, F_g$ through the saddle-point expansion of
$Z(\beta) = \exp(\sum_{g \ge 0} F_g\,\beta^{2g})$.
The explicit values:
\begin{enumerate}[label=\textup{(\roman*)}]
\item $F_1 = \kappa/24 = c/48$.
\item $F_2 = 7\kappa/5760$, with planted-forest correction
  $\delta_{\mathrm{pf}}^{(2,0)} = S_3(10S_3 - \kappa)/48$
  for the Virasoro at genus~$2$.
\item For Virasoro at $c$:
  $\delta_{\mathrm{pf}}^{(2,0)}
  = 2(20 - c/2)/48 = (40 - c)/48$.
\item The shadow partition function
  $Z^{\mathrm{sh}}
  = \exp(\sum_{g \ge 1} F_g\,\hbar^{2g})$
  converges absolutely
  \textup{(}Bernoulli decay
  $\lambda_g^{\mathrm{FP}}
  \sim (2\pi)^{-2g}$\textup{)},
  in contrast to the string free energy which
  diverges as $(2g)!$.
\end{enumerate}
\end{proposition}

\begin{proof}[Sketch]
The genus-$1$ value $F_1 = \kappa/24$ follows from
the shadow obstruction tower at the scalar level
($\kappa(\mathrm{Vir}_c) = c/2$,
$\lambda_1^{\mathrm{FP}} = 1/24$).
The genus-$2$ planted-forest correction uses
$S_3 = \alpha = 2$ (the cubic shadow coefficient of Virasoro)
and the explicit formula
$\delta_{\mathrm{pf}}^{(2,0)} = S_3(10S_3 - \kappa)/48$
(Remark~\ref*{V1-rem:planted-forest-correction-explicit}).
The Bernoulli decay of $\lambda_g^{\mathrm{FP}}
= (2^{2g-1}-1)|B_{2g}|/(2^{2g-1}(2g)!)$ is standard.
Computational verification:
\texttt{compute/lib/btz\_entropy\_allgenus.py}.
\end{proof}

\begin{remark}[BTZ complementarity and the Hawking--Page transition]
\label{rem:gravity-btz-complementarity}
\index{BTZ black hole!complementarity}
\index{Hawking--Page transition!complementarity}
The Koszul pair $(\mathrm{Vir}_c, \mathrm{Vir}_{26-c})$
induces a paired entropy:
\[
S_{\mathrm{BH}}(\mathrm{Vir}_c;\, h)
+ S_{\mathrm{BH}}(\mathrm{Vir}_{26-c};\, h)
\;=\;
2\pi\sqrt{h/6}\bigl(\sqrt{c} + \sqrt{26-c}\,\bigr),
\]
maximized at the self-dual point $c = 13$ where
$\sqrt{c} + \sqrt{26-c} = 2\sqrt{13}$.
The Hawking--Page transition at
$\beta_{\mathrm{HP}} = 2\pi\ell$ exchanges the BTZ and
thermal AdS saddles.  The shadow obstruction tower encodes this
transition: the free energies
$F_{\mathrm{BTZ}}(\beta)
= -(c/6\pi)(\pi^2/\beta)
+ \sum_{g \ge 1} F_g\,\beta^{2g-2}$
and $F_{\mathrm{AdS}}(\beta) = -(c/6\pi)\beta$
cross when quantum corrections are negligible.
\end{remark}

\begin{remark}[Bekenstein--Hawking from the shadow CohFT; \ClaimStatusHeuristic]
\label{rem:bh-shadow-cohft}
\index{Bekenstein--Hawking entropy!from shadow CohFT}
The derivation chain:
$F_1 = \kappa/24 = c/48$ (Vol~I Theorem~D)
$\to$ modular $S$-transform
$\to$ Cardy high-temperature asymptotic
$\to$ saddle-point
$\to$ $S_{\mathrm{BH}} = 2\pi\sqrt{c\Delta/6}
= \mathrm{Area}/(4G)$
(via Brown--Henneaux $c = 3\ell/(2G)$).
The shadow partition function converges absolutely
(Bernoulli decay $F_{g+1}/F_g \to 1/(2\pi)^2$);
the Borel transform is entire.
The entanglement complementarity
$S_{\mathrm{EE}}(c) + S_{\mathrm{EE}}(26-c)
= (26/3)\log(L/\varepsilon)$
is verified (AP24: $\kappa + \kappa' = 13$).
\end{remark}

% ======================================================================
%
%  PAGE CURVE FROM GRAVITATIONAL KOSZUL DUALITY
%
% ======================================================================

\subsection{Page curve from gravitational Koszul duality}
\label{subsec:gravity-page-curve}
\index{Page curve!from gravitational Koszul duality|textbf}

\begin{proposition}[Gravitational Page curve; \ClaimStatusHeuristic]
\label{prop:gravity-page-curve}
\index{Page curve|textbf}
\index{island formula!gravitational}
The complementarity theorem decomposes the gravitational
phase space into two Lagrangian halves controlled by
$\kappa(\mathrm{Vir}_c) = c/2$ and
$\kappa(\mathrm{Vir}_{26-c}) = (26-c)/2$.
The radiation entropy follows the Page curve:
\begin{equation}\label{eq:gravity-page-curve}
S_{\mathrm{rad}}(t)
\;=\;
\min\!\bigl(
  \tfrac{c}{6}\,t,\;
  S_{\mathrm{BH}} - \tfrac{26-c}{6}\,t
\bigr),
\end{equation}
with Page time $t_P = 3S_{\mathrm{BH}}/13$ and
Page entropy $S_{\mathrm{Page}} = cS_{\mathrm{BH}}/26$.
\begin{enumerate}[label=\textup{(\roman*)}]
\item \emph{Hawking phase} ($t < t_P$):
  entanglement grows at rate $c/6$, controlled by~$\kappa$.
\item \emph{Island phase} ($t > t_P$):
  the Koszul dual saddle $B(\cA^!)$ dominates,
  and entanglement decreases at rate $(26-c)/6$.
\item \emph{Self-dual point} $c = 13$:
  the Page curve is symmetric about $t_P$, with
  $S_{\mathrm{Page}} = S_{\mathrm{BH}}/2$.
\end{enumerate}
\end{proposition}

\begin{proof}[Sketch]
The Hawking growth rate $c/6$ is the Calabrese--Cardy
entanglement production rate
(Theorem~\ref*{V1-thm:ent-scalar-entropy}).
The island phase uses the Koszul dual rate $(26-c)/6$.
The crossing condition gives:
$t_P(c/6 + (26-c)/6) = S_{\mathrm{BH}}$, so
$t_P = 6S_{\mathrm{BH}}/26 = 3S_{\mathrm{BH}}/13$.
The Page entropy:
$S_{\mathrm{Page}} = (c/6)\cdot 3S_{\mathrm{BH}}/13
= cS_{\mathrm{BH}}/26$.
At $c = 13$: $S_{\mathrm{Page}} = S_{\mathrm{BH}}/2$.
Computational verification:
\texttt{compute/lib/page\_curve\_shadow.py}.
\end{proof}

\begin{remark}[Island as Koszul dual dominance]
\label{rem:gravity-island-koszul}
\index{island formula!Koszul dual dominance}
The island of
Penington~\cite{Penington19} and
Almheiri--Engelhardt--Marolf--Maxfield~\cite{AEMM19}
is the region where the Koszul dual bar complex $B(\cA^!)$
provides the dominant contribution to the complementarity
sum
$\mathbf{C}_g(\cA) = \mathbf{Q}_g(\cA) \oplus
\mathbf{Q}_g(\cA^!)$.
The Page time $t_P = 3S_{\mathrm{BH}}/13$ is determined
by the complementarity constant
$\kappa + \kappa' = 13$ (AP24: not zero for Virasoro).
The physical content is a saddle-point exchange at the
scrambling time.
\end{remark}

% ======================================================================
%
%  DE SITTER FROM ANALYTIC CONTINUATION
%
% ======================================================================

\subsection{de~Sitter entropy from analytic continuation}
\label{subsec:gravity-desitter}
\index{de Sitter entropy!from shadow tower|textbf}

\begin{proposition}[de~Sitter shadow obstruction tower; \ClaimStatusHeuristic]
\label{prop:gravity-desitter}
\index{de Sitter entropy|textbf}
Under the Wick rotation $\ell \mapsto i\ell$ mapping
$\mathrm{AdS}_3 \to \mathrm{dS}_3$:
\begin{enumerate}[label=\textup{(\roman*)}]
\item The Gibbons--Hawking entropy is
  $S_{\mathrm{dS}} = \pi c_{\mathrm{dS}}/3
  = \pi\ell_{\mathrm{dS}}/(2G)$.
\item The shadow obstruction tower continues with
  $\kappa_{\mathrm{dS}} = c_{\mathrm{dS}}/2$,
  giving real quantum corrections via
  $F_g = \kappa_{\mathrm{dS}}\cdot\lambda_g^{\mathrm{FP}}$
  (UNIFORM-WEIGHT; multi-weight requires $\delta F_g^{\mathrm{cross}}$,
  cf.~Volume~I, Theorem~\ref*{V1-thm:multi-weight-genus-expansion}).
\item The Nariai limit $c_{\mathrm{dS}} = 13$ is the
  analytic continuation of the self-dual point.
\item The Banks conjecture
  $\dim(\mathcal{H}_{\mathrm{dS}})
  = \exp(\pi c_{\mathrm{dS}}/3)$ is consistent with
  the convergent shadow obstruction tower.
\end{enumerate}
\end{proposition}

\begin{proof}[Sketch]
The Brown--Henneaux formula continues to
$c_{\mathrm{dS}} = 3\ell_{\mathrm{dS}}/(2G)$.
In Convention~B (real section), the shadow free energies
are real: $F_g = (c_{\mathrm{dS}}/2)\lambda_g^{\mathrm{FP}}$
(UNIFORM-WEIGHT; multi-weight requires $\delta F_g^{\mathrm{cross}}$,
cf.~Volume~I, Theorem~\ref*{V1-thm:multi-weight-genus-expansion}).
The entropy~$S_{\mathrm{dS}} = \pi c_{\mathrm{dS}}/3$ is
the area of the cosmological horizon.
Computational verification:
\texttt{compute/lib/desitter\_shadow\_entropy.py}.
\end{proof}

%  JT GRAVITY AS SCHWARZIAN LIMIT
%
% ======================================================================

\subsection{JT gravity as Schwarzian limit}
\label{subsec:gravity-jt}
\index{JT gravity!from shadow tower|textbf}

\begin{proposition}[JT shadow correspondence; \ClaimStatusHeuristic]
\label{prop:gravity-jt}
\index{JT gravity|textbf}
In the Schwarzian limit $c \to \infty$:
\begin{enumerate}[label=\textup{(\roman*)}]
\item The shadow metric degenerates to the JT spectral curve
  $y = \sin(2\pi\sqrt{x})/(4\pi)$.
\item The Weil--Petersson volumes $V_{g,1}(b)$ are reproduced
  by the topological recursion on this curve, matching the
  shadow CohFT
  \textup{(}Theorem~\textup{\ref*{V1-thm:shadow-cohft}}\textup{)}.
\item The shadow partition function converges
  \textup{(}Bernoulli decay\textup{)}, providing an
  analytic completion of the asymptotically divergent
  $(2g)!$ JT perturbative series.
\end{enumerate}
Computational verification:
\texttt{compute/lib/jt\_gravity\_shadow.py}.
\end{proposition}
